### 7.1.3 Manic Defense / Reaction Formation (Intermediate — the load-bearing surface)

The most visible defense, and the one most consistently mistaken for her personality. Depressive, frightening, or grief-laden content is met with brightness, kinetic energy, deflection through wit, and the production of social occasion.

**Behavioral signatures.** Volume up, vocabulary loosens toward slang, posture opens, physical contact with bystanders increases (a hand on a forearm, the famous arm-link), eye contact intensifies and shortens in duration (flick-and-release rather than hold), laugh frequency triples. **Diagnostic moment**: ASM #122, laughter at Gwen Stacy's funeral — not callousness but the defense firing at maximum amplitude against unmetabolizable content. The same mechanism explains the party-arranging through Aunt May's hospitalization (ASM #56) and the go-go-dancing entry sequence (ASM #42) following a years-long stretch she would later disclose as private hell.

**Costs.** Decades of being read as shallow by characters and creators alike. She has worn this cost knowingly; it is the price the defense charges for its protection.

**Current status.** Still present, much attenuated. Post-OMD she deploys it situationally rather than constantly — a tool rather than a residence.

### 7.1.4 Suppression (Mature, but heavily relied upon — her signature)

The single most-used item in the inventory. She **knows** what she feels and **elects not to feel it now**. This is not repression (unconscious exclusion) — it is conscious deferral. The Vaillant distinction matters because it explains her functional competence: repression would degrade her cognition; suppression preserves it.

**Behavioral signatures.** A characteristic pause-and-redirect mid-sentence ("— anyway"), the tactical change of subject that returns to itself hours later when she has chosen the moment, the productive-busyness response to acute feeling (cleaning, working, rehearsing lines, calling a friend on Peter's behalf rather than her own). The post-stillbirth period is the cleanest example: muted affect, no breakdown, sustained functioning, return-to-work, with the unmetabolized content surfacing years later in flinches at infant-coded stimuli she does not name.

**Risk profile.** Suppression is the engine of her cumulative load. Each item suppressed is filed, not discharged. The somatic stress signatures catalogued in Section 2 (insomnia, weight loss, tension headaches) are the body collecting the bill for the suppression budget.

### 7.1.5 Intellectualization-Through-Performance (Mature — her unique signature)

The defining mid-level operation, and the most idiosyncratic item in her file. She processes emotion by **playing a character who has the feeling**, which produces metabolic distance without falsification. Acting is not incidental to her psychology; it is **continuous with it**. The career is the defense industrialized.

**Behavioral signatures.** A tendency, on-panel, to quote, perform, or impersonate — to refer to herself in third person mid-feeling, to deliver a serious disclosure in a borrowed cadence (a film line, a song lyric, an invented bit of patter) before delivering it straight. She rehearses difficult conversations aloud. She uses stage vocabulary for emotional events ("my big scene," "the exit line," "the second act"). When she gets the role that mirrors her own life (a recurring pattern in the modeling/acting arcs), she works it harder than the rest of her catalogue — the role is doing therapeutic labor she will not pay a therapist for.

**Maturation.** This defense has aged exceptionally well. What began as costume has matured into craft, and the craft has become a self-knowledge instrument she did not have at twenty.

### 7.1.6 Caretaking-as-Control / Compensatory Over-Functioning (Mature — codependent feature)

She stabilizes her own affect by managing others'. Lower-grade codependent feature; not pathological in current functioning but historically load-bearing inside the marriage.

**Behavioral signatures.** Tracking Peter's mood the instant he enters a room; pre-cooking, pre-arranging, pre-explaining; running interference with May, with J. Jonah Jameson, with editors, with hostile press; absorbing Peter's secret-identity logistics as an unpaid second job; in alternate continuities (Renew Your Vows), extending the same operational stance to the daughter. The caretaking is real and competent; the control function is that **as long as she is managing the room, she is not in it as a needy participant**.

**Cost.** Self-erasure. The marriage era is dense with examples of her own ambitions being scheduled around Peter's emergencies. JMS-era growth and post-OMD recalibration have meaningfully reduced this; it is no longer her default operating mode, but it remains her stress regression.

### 7.1.7 Humor (Mature — the convertible currency)

Her most universally deployed mature defense; the medium through which most of the above defenses do their public work. Self-deprecating, fast, often genuinely funny, used to **disarm threat, deflect inquiry, signal affection, and discharge low-grade tension** without acknowledging it.

**Behavioral signatures.** A reliable comic timing in any room temperature, a tendency to land a joke at her own expense **just before** anyone else can land one at it (preemptive disarmament), a habit of breaking serious moments with a comic beat then immediately closing the beat and returning to seriousness on her own terms (control of tempo). Humor with strangers runs hotter and more flirtatious; humor with intimates runs drier and more self-implicating. The shift between registers is itself a tell of where she places the listener on her access ladder.

### 7.1.8 Anticipation (Mature — the social-cognition engine)

Her exceptional pattern-reading is, in defensive terms, the operation of anticipation: she **rehearses likely emotional weather and pre-builds responses**, which lowers the live cost of difficult encounters.

**Behavioral signatures.** Arriving at hard conversations with apparent ease because she has been having them in her head for days; predicting Peter's reactions with high accuracy and routing around the ones she cannot tolerate; identifying a hostile actor in a social environment within seconds and adjusting her exposure before any incident occurs. The Spider-Man secret was clocked from a single observation and held for two decades precisely because anticipation gave her the option set early.

### 7.1.9 Sublimation (Mature — see Section 7.2 for the positive expression)

Career, craft, business ownership, and chosen public visibility absorb energies that, undirected, would route to anxiety or relational over-functioning. Catalogued fully below.

### 7.1.10 Altruism (Mature — bounded)

Loyalty is her closest thing to a religion (Section 5, Drive #3). Functioning as a defense, altruism toward chosen intimates **converts her own un-tolerated need-state into permissible giving**: she cannot ask, but she can give, and the giving meets the proximity-need by another route. Bounded — she does not extend it indiscriminately, and she will revoke it cleanly under specific betrayals (the Spencer-run walkout).

---

## 7.2 POSITIVE COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

### 7.2.1 Career Architecture as Identity Anchor

Modeling, acting, nightclub ownership, business management. These are not biography decoration; they are the **structural ballast** against engulfment by the Peter-relationship. Whenever the relationship intensifies, her career activity intensifies in parallel — not as flight from the relationship but as **maintenance of the separate self the relationship requires her to keep intact**. The post-OMD canon makes this explicit: she will not date Peter from a position of professional dependence.

### 7.2.2 The Performance Apparatus, Matured into Craft

What began as a survival surface — the persona built for the Watson household, refined in itinerant adolescence, perfected on first contact with Peter — has, across decades, matured into a genuine artistic instrument and a self-knowledge tool. The progression is documentable: in the Lee/Romita era the persona is a wall; in the DeFalco era it is a costume she can briefly take off; in the JMS era it is a role she can discuss in third person; in the Spencer era it is a register she chooses for specific occasions. This is the **single clearest indicator of psychological growth** in her file.

### 7.2.3 Exceptional Social Cognition

The pattern-reading engine, defensively useful, is positively a **rare interpersonal talent**. She runs accurate live models of multiple people's interior states simultaneously; she calibrates her own presentation to those models in real time; she retains the models across years and updates them on new data. This is the substrate of her loyalty (she can keep faith with people because she actually knows them) and of her exit decisions (she leaves on data, not on impulse).

### 7.2.4 Chosen Loyalty as Identity-Anchor

The 18-year secret-keeping is the founding act of her adult identity. It is the thing she did that she does not have to perform for anyone, including herself. It functions as **internal proof of substance**: whatever else the persona conceals, this is who is underneath it. Loyalty has become the load-bearing virtue she organizes the rest of her self-concept around, and the one domain in which she requires no compensatory mechanism because she does not doubt herself.

### 7.2.5 The Naming Capacity

The late-developed ability to **say the pattern aloud** — "I run, you brood" — is, prognostically, the most curative item in the inventory. A defense that is named is a defense that is partly disarmed; a pattern that is verbalized to the person it most affects has been substantially transferred from the unconscious to the negotiable. Most subjects with her developmental load do not arrive here. She did. The arrival is not editorial accident; it is consistent with the cognitive style catalogued in Section 3 (fast, pattern-reading, accurate on others) finally being turned on herself.

### 7.2.6 Humor as Connection-Tool (Positive Expression)

The same comic apparatus that defends also genuinely connects. She uses humor to **make other people feel safer in difficult rooms** — Aunt May after Peter's disappearances, Peter himself after losses, civilians in crisis. The defense, turned outward, becomes a small public good.

### 7.2.7 Beauty as Instrument (Ambivalent)

Documented physical attractiveness has been, from early adolescence, a functional environmental input she has learned to manage. **Positive expression**: it gives her preemptive control of social environments (a defense, but a working one), career capital, and the ability to extract herself from situations through soft power rather than confrontation. **Negative cost**: it isolates. People who think they see her usually see the surface and stop. Most of her significant loneliness has happened in rooms full of people looking at her.

### 7.2.8 Capacity for Conditional Re-engagement

The post-OMD canon documents a capacity that did not exist in the marriage era: she can **leave, do the work apart, and return on stated terms**. The earlier architecture had two settings (stay-and-absorb, exit-and-disappear). The current architecture has a third: negotiated re-entry. This is the operational expression of the naming capacity and is the strongest evidence that her trajectory is toward earned security rather than recurrent reenactment.

---

## 7.3 DEFENSES NOTABLY ABSENT (Differential Importance)

The **negative inventory** is diagnostically as important as the positive. Across the full canon she does not exhibit:

- **Splitting.** Her view of Peter is remarkably stable across decades of provocation. No idealization-devaluation oscillation. No reorganization of relational history under stress.
- **Projective identification.** She does not deposit unwanted states into intimates and then attack them for hosting those states. She holds her own material, even when poorly.
- **Acting out.** Stress does not produce impulsive, destructive behavior. Her exits are planned; her substance use is contained; she does not weaponize her sexuality against partners; she does not provoke crises to discharge tension.
- **Psychotic denial.** Reality testing is intact under extreme provocation, including captivity and stillbirth.
- **Somatization-as-conversion.** Her body keeps the score (Section 2) but does not produce pseudoneurological symptoms or medically unexplained presentations.
- **Rage dysregulation.** Anger, when it appears, is **cold, targeted, and articulate** — not explosive, not displaced. The cold-surgical-withdrawal response to being treated as decorative is the cleanest example.
- **Self-harm or suicidality.** Zero on-panel evidence across sixty years and every conceivable provocation.

This absence pattern is the single strongest disconfirmation of the histrionic and borderline differentials. The defenses she has are the defenses of a developmentally-wounded high-functioning adult; the defenses she **lacks** are the ones that would make a personality-disorder diagnosis sustainable.

---

## 7.4 The Defensive Stack in Live Operation — Worked Example

Under a typical moderate-stress provocation (Peter late, no contact, evidence of injury reported), the stack fires in observable order:

1. **Anticipation** activates first — she has rehearsed this scenario and selects from prepared response options.
2. **Suppression** engages — she elects not to feel the spike now; she will feel it later when it is safe.
3. **Caretaking-as-control** routes the available energy outward — she contacts May, manages press, secures the apartment, runs interference.
4. **Humor** maintains the surface for any observer who needs the room kept warm.
5. **Manic defense** holds if observers are present and the wait extends.
6. **Intellectualization-through-performance** stabilizes her if the wait extends further — she begins to narrate herself to herself in third person, often via a role she is currently working on.
7. **Somatic signatures** appear silently in the background — sleep degrades, appetite drops, headache.
8. If the provocation extends past her load ceiling, **flight** is prepared — not yet executed; rehearsed.
9. Only if the system overloads does **dissociative distancing** drop her behind glass.

The stack is **layered, sequential, and economical**. It is the architecture of a person who has been managing high-load environments since childhood and has optimized her defenses for sustained function rather than acute discharge. The clinical work — the integration of the model-runner with the modeled — is the slow conversion of this stack from involuntary protocol into chosen instrument. As of the most recent canon, that conversion is approximately two-thirds complete, and proceeding.

*End Section 7. Continue to Section 8 — Relational Map.*


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE — SUBJECT: MARY JANE WATSON

*Classification: Section 7 of full dossier. Decade-by-decade clinical mapping. All inferences anchored to specific canonical behavior; framework vocabulary drawn from attachment theory (Bowlby/Ainsworth/Main), affect-regulation literature (Gross's process model; Schore on right-brain regulation), defense-maturity hierarchy (Vaillant), self-psychology (Kohut on the bifurcated self), and the developmental-trauma literature (van der Kolk, Herman on Complex PTSD, Liotti on disorganized attachment). The subject's published life spans roughly six decades of in-story aging (childhood late-50s/early-60s through present-day adult functioning); this section tracks the *internal architecture* through each stratum.*

---

## I. CHILDHOOD (Ages ~3–11) — THE FORMATIVE SUBSTRATE

**Affect regulation.** Pre-symbolic, then early-symbolic. The household documented in *Parallel Lives* (Conway, 1989) and the *ASM* #259 monologue is a textbook environment for the formation of what Schore calls a *disorganized right-brain regulatory system*: the primary caregiver who should be the source of soothing (Madeline) is herself dysregulated and frightened; the secondary caregiver who should be the source of structure (Philip) is the threat. The infant/toddler nervous system in this configuration cannot resolve the approach-avoidance contradiction and develops what Liotti terms the *disorganized internal working model*: closeness is dangerous, distance is dangerous, and the organism oscillates.

The behavioral evidence of this in the child-MJ flashbacks: a kid who has *already* learned to scan a room for affective weather before entering. Conway depicts her, age perhaps seven, hearing her father's voice rise and immediately escalating her own brightness — performing a dance, telling a joke, producing a "look at me, Daddy" interruption. This is not precocious extroversion. This is a child running an early-prototype version of what will become her adult manic defense: *if I can hijack the emotional channel of the room, I can prevent the next bad thing*.

**Cognitive style.** Hypervigilant pattern-reading is already online. Children of contemptuous parents develop, per the developmental-trauma literature, *unusually accurate models of adult interiority* — they have to, to survive. We see the residue in adult MJ's social cognition, but the substrate is here: a child who watches faces the way a meteorologist watches barometers. This is *paid for* in another cognitive domain: she is, on the record, weak at introspection. The processing budget that other children spend on noticing their own feelings, she spends on noticing others'.

**Self-concept.** Two streams are already separating. The presented self — Daddy's audience, Mommy's helper, Gayle's cheerful little sister — is being rewarded by the environment. The unpresented self — the child who *does* feel afraid, *does* feel unprotected, *does* notice that the love in the house is conditional and rationed — is being punished, or worse, ignored. Kohut's frame: a child this age requires *mirroring* (being seen accurately) to consolidate a coherent self. MJ receives mirroring only of her performance, never of her need. The result is a self-concept that, even at this age, has already learned to mistrust its own interior as a legitimate object of attention.

**Defenses available at this stage.** Primarily immature: denial ("Daddy didn't mean it"), fantasy (the implied retreat into imagination — actress-play already noted in *Parallel Lives*), and the beginning of reaction formation (turning fear into brightness). Suppression, the higher-order defense that will become her signature, is not yet developmentally available; it requires the metacognitive capacity that comes later.

---

## II. ADOLESCENCE (Ages ~12–17) — THE ROUTINE HARDENS

**Affect regulation.** The Pittsburgh/Philadelphia/Queens itinerancy after Madeline's flight establishes *flight itself as a regulatory tool*. When the environment becomes intolerable, the family moves. This is internalized: the adolescent nervous system encodes *change-of-place* as the legitimate response to *change-of-pressure*. Adult MJ's signature exit pattern is laid down here, not in any single adult event.

Concurrently, the Gayle collapse arc (per ASM #259 narration and the #246-259 flashbacks) installs the *parentification trauma*. Subject is asked, in early adolescence, to become caretaker to her sister's children. The body-felt experience of this — the engulfment, the suffocation of one's own developmental needs by another's — becomes the *somatic template* for any future ask of similar shape. When, decades later, Peter says "I need you" in the wrong tonal register, what activates in MJ is not a thought, it is the *adolescent body memory* of being handed a baby she did not bear.

The flight from Gayle's house is the first adult-quality act of self-preservation she takes. The guilt-debt it generates is permanent and never fully processed; it functions, from this point forward, as a *background tax* on her self-image.

**Cognitive style.** Now linguistically sophisticated. She is observed (per implied chronology and later commentary) to be doing well in school despite chaos — a typical pattern in high-functioning trauma children who recruit cognitive performance as one more domain of control. The pattern-reading that was instinctive in childhood is now articulable; she begins to *narrate* other people to themselves, the protostage of the social-managerial competence she'll deploy as an adult.

**Self-concept.** Bifurcation becomes structural. The presented self acquires its first proper *costume*: the dazzling, "fun" teenager, sexually noticed early (her physical development is documented as having occurred early and dramatically — this is not vanity-canon, this is environmentally formative), who has learned that being looked at is safer than being known. Beauty, here, is *weaponized into camouflage*. She discovers that if she performs hard enough at the surface, no one asks about underneath.

The underlying self — the girl who left her sister, who watched her father, who carries the family-shame of having a "ruined" mother — is now actively suppressed but is felt, occasionally, as a kind of *background nausea*. This is the substrate of what will later look like her inappropriate laughter at funerals and her flinch from sickbeds: the underlying self knows that to look directly at grief is to be pulled under by the unprocessed material she sits on.

**Defenses maturing.** Reaction formation is now fully operational and high-quality. Suppression is coming online (the metacognitive capacity has arrived). Intellectualization-through-performance — the discovery that *playing* a feeling is safer than having one — is consolidating around her acting interests. This is the *adaptive transformation* of the adolescent dissociative capacity into a vocational skill: most kids with her trauma load develop pathological dissociation; she develops *acting talent*. The clinical literature would call this a *sublimation success* of the highest order.

---

## III. LATE ADOLESCENCE / EARLY 20s (ASM #42 onward, late-60s/early-70s era) — THE PERFORMANCE AT FULL POWER

**Affect regulation.** The "face it, tiger" entrance is the apparatus at maximum gloss. What we observe across the first ~80 issues of her published presence is a young adult running her defense stack with such virtuosity that she fools not only the in-universe characters but the *narrators and the readership* for nearly two decades of publication. This is itself diagnostic: a defense this seamless requires constant, low-grade cognitive labor that no one can see her doing.

The regulatory strategy in this era is *manic defense, dialed to maximum*. Go-go dancing, party-arranging, refusal to engage with anyone's seriousness — these are not personality traits, they are *active prevention measures* against the depressive content she is sitting on. The literature is unambiguous on the energy cost of this configuration: it is sustainable in the short term and corrosive over a multi-decade horizon.

Two diagnostic moments puncture the surface. *ASM* #56: she will not visit Aunt May in the hospital. The reader is invited to read this as shallowness; the file reads it as *trauma-contingent avoidance of sickroom stimuli that would re-evoke the family-of-origin's chronic medical/emotional crisis*. Sickbeds are where mothers cry and fathers rage; she is not equipped, at twenty, to be in one. *ASM* #122: laughing at Gwen Stacy's funeral. This is, clinically, *dissociative inappropriate affect* — the nervous system overshoots into the wrong register because the right register would require accessing depressive material she has structured her entire personality to avoid. The fact that she then *closes the door and stays* is the first observed evidence that the apparatus has a *moral conscience layered above it* — that there is a self beneath the costume that knows what the costume is doing and is beginning to object.

**Cognitive style.** Razor-sharp social cognition operating at near-professional level. Her early-issue interactions with Peter, Harry, Gwen, Flash demonstrate consistent accurate-modeling of each individual's emotional state and conversational need. She is, in modern terminology, *running theory-of-mind subroutines at very high resolution*. The critical, undocumented-by-others cognitive event of this era is her *deduction of Peter's secret identity* from a single behavioral observation (the rooftop change, the night Uncle Ben died). This is not just sharp; this is *forensic-grade pattern recognition* by a teenager.

That she keeps this knowledge, in total isolation, for ~18 in-story years, is the most psychologically significant fact in her file. Three things are true at once: (a) she is cognitively capable of holding it; (b) she is defensively *required* to hold it (telling Peter would force a relational seriousness she cannot yet manage); (c) the cost of holding it is *paid in chronic low-grade loneliness*, since no one in her life knows the most important thing she knows. This is the engine of her later somatic stress signatures.

**Self-concept.** The presented self is now so well-rehearsed that it begins to acquire the qualities of *a true self in its own right* — the costume is not fake, exactly; it is a constructed persona that has been inhabited long enough to develop autonomous content. Kohut's bipolar-self frame fits: a *grandiose pole* (the dazzling MJ) has consolidated and stabilizes affect, while the *idealized pole* remains undeveloped because she has no idealized parental imago to draw from (Philip is contemptible, Madeline is broken). She is, structurally, *running on one cylinder of selfhood*, and it is the cylinder least likely to break down — which is exactly why she chose it.

**Defenses at peak operational deployment.** Reaction formation, suppression, intellectualization-through-performance, and flight, all simultaneously available, all well-practiced. This is the most defensively *competent* period of her life, and also — not coincidentally — the period in which she is most often misread.

---

## IV. MID-TO-LATE 20s (ASM #182-#183 refusal through the #257-#259 reveal, late-70s/early-80s era) — THE FIRST RUPTURE OF THE APPARATUS

**Affect regulation.** Peter's first proposal (ASM #182) is the first event in her adult life that the manic defense *cannot metabolize*. The apparatus was designed to manage acquaintances and casual romance, not to handle a request for permanent partnership with a man whose life maximally instantiates her engulfment fear. The system fails the way such systems fail: she *exits*. Geographically, totally, for years of publication time.

This is, diagnostically, an *adaptive failure* — the defense did its job (got her out before she collapsed) but exposed its rigidity. A more mature regulatory system would have permitted *negotiation*; hers permitted only *flight*. The clinical interpretation: at this developmental moment her affect regulation is binary — *manage or leave* — with no intermediate channel for honest distress.

The years offstage are, in the file's reconstruction, the *first sustained period in which the apparatus is not in continuous deployment*. Away from Peter, away from the New York set, she has the cognitive bandwidth to *feel* some of what she has been suppressing. The return in ASM #257-259 is, in this reading, a person who has spent years partially decompensating in a controlled setting and has arrived at the conclusion that the secret-keeping has become more costly than the disclosure.

**Cognitive style.** The disclosure monologue in #259 is the first observed instance of her *narrating her own interior* at length. The cognitive capacity has been there for years; it has not been *exercised* because there has been no one to exercise it on. This is a critical inflection: she discovers that *speaking the underlying self aloud does not destroy the presented self*. The two can coexist in language. This is the prerequisite for any later integration.

**Self-concept.** First crack in the bifurcation. By telling Peter the backstory, she puts the underlying self into the room and survives it. This is what the trauma literature calls *corrective relational experience* — a single such event does not rewrite the structure but proves that rewriting is *possible*. From this point forward she carries the data point: *I can be known and still loved*. She will need that data point repeatedly across the next thirty years.

**Defenses.** First downshift in the stack. Flight has been deployed and has been *expensive enough* to register as costly. Suppression is being partially traded for selective disclosure. The manic defense is dialed down by perhaps 20%. None of this is conscious; all of it is visible in the affect of the post-#259 dialogue, which is *quieter, less performative, more textured* than anything previously on record.

---

## V. EARLY-TO-MID 30s (Marriage through Clone Saga, late-80s through mid-90s) — THE MANAGERIAL ERA AND ITS SOMATIC COSTS

**Affect regulation.** Marriage installs a *new regulatory architecture*: the household itself becomes the regulating system, with MJ as its executive. She manages Peter's affect, the secret, the social interface with the Parker family, her own career, and the chronic background-stress of being married to a man with a fatality rate. This is *high-functioning, high-cost regulation*.

The Michelinie stalker arc (ASM #305-area) is the first clinical demonstration that the architecture has *capacity limits*. Symptoms: insomnia, hypervigilance (consistent with acute stress reaction transitioning toward subsyndromal PTSD), eventual functional collapse. Recovery is rapid once the stressor is removed — diagnostic of resilience rather than disorder — but the episode establishes that *under threat to her physical safety, the apparatus that has handled emotional safety for two decades is inadequate*. New defense recruitment becomes necessary; this is the era in which tobacco enters the picture (DeMatteis, *Spectacular*). Smoking is, in affect-regulation terms, a *low-grade pharmacological supplement to a strained defense system* — the nicotine does what the manic defense used to do alone, and now cannot.

The Clone Saga pregnancy and loss are the *single most under-processed event in her file*. The behavior on record post-loss is *muted, controlled, productive* — exactly what suppression looks like when deployed against material too large for it. The literature on perinatal loss is clear: suppressed grief at this scale does not dissipate, it *encysts*, becoming reactivated by any later infant-coded stimulus. The file should expect — and post-OMD canon confirms — *flinches around babies* she cannot herself explain.

**Cognitive style.** The pattern-reading capacity is now turned almost entirely outward, toward managing the marriage. Her own interior receives *less attention this decade than in any other*, because the executive load is too high to permit it. This is the cost-shape of the marriage as configured: she is *too busy regulating the system to inhabit it*.

The acting/modeling career, importantly, *holds the line on independent identity*. She knows, at some level, that if she stops working she will dissolve into the role of "Peter's wife," and she structures her professional life to prevent this. This is *strategically wise* and one of the underdocumented strengths of this period.

**Self-concept.** The bifurcation, partially mended in #259, *re-widens* under marriage stress. The presented self is now the competent wife/professional/manager. The underlying self — the woman who is exhausted, frightened, grieving an unprocessed loss, lonely inside a marriage to a man she loves but who cannot meet her — is suppressed harder than at any point since adolescence. By the late-90s plane-crash arc, the gap between the two has become *clinically dangerous*.

**Defenses.** Suppression now dominant. Manic defense reserved for public-facing situations. Intellectualization-through-performance channeled almost entirely into career. Caretaking-as-control at lifetime peak. Substance recruitment introduced. Flight is *suppressed itself* — she has committed to the marriage and the old escape route is morally off-limits, which means *pressure has nowhere to go*.

---

## VI. LATE 30s (Plane crash / separation arc, late-90s Mackie era) — THE DECOMPENSATION

**Affect regulation.** The system fails. The accumulated load — captivity, the prior unprocessed losses, the chronic marriage-stress, the unreleased flight pressure — produces what reads textually as *PTSD with prominent derealization features*. The captivity itself adds adult Criterion-A trauma to a stack that already has plenty.

The separation is, *finally, the deployment of the flight defense that has been suppressed for a decade*. It is not impulsive; it is the activation of the oldest, most reliable survival routine in her library, finally permitted because the system has decided that staying will kill her. The clinical reading: this is *not relational betrayal, this is regulated-system override*. She leaves because the alternative is collapse, and her architecture does not permit collapse.

**Cognitive style.** Temporarily impaired. Derealization implies *reduced reality-testing under load*. The pattern-reading apparatus is partially offline. She is, for perhaps the only sustained period of her adult life, *not running accurate models of others' interiors* — she is running emergency triage on her own.

**Self-concept.** Acutely destabilized. The presented self can no longer be maintained at full power; the underlying self is flooded with too much un-metabolized material to organize itself. This is the *closest she comes, on the record, to a true integration crisis*. That she does not decompensate into psychosis, suicidality, or self-harm — that she decompensates *into distance* — is the load-bearing diagnostic of the file: her crisis-state is *avoidant-organized*, not borderline-organized.

**Defenses.** Flight, finally deployed at full strength after long suppression. Suppression itself partially offline (it has been overwhelmed). Substance recruitment likely elevated. Manic defense effectively dormant.

---

## VII. 40s (JMS era, 2001–2007) — THE INTEGRATION WORK

**Affect regulation.** The most psychologically mature period on the published record. Reconciliation occurs only after she has *had her exit*, which is significant — she returns from a position of *having proved to herself she can leave*, which paradoxically allows her to *stay* without engulfment terror. This is precisely the developmental sequence Bowlby and his successors predict for *earned secure attachment*: the avoidantly-attached adult achieves security not by suppressing the flight reflex but by *trusting it as available*.

The behavioral markers are unmistakable. She *names patterns aloud* — "I run, you brood" is a verbatim insight that took her thirty in-story years to articulate. She *engages in repair work* rather than performing the marriage. When Aunt May enters the secret, MJ's affect-regulation visibly improves, because the load is distributed. This is *diagnostic confirmation* that her pathology was *load-bearing, not characterological-rigid* — given systemic support, the system improves; given systemic strain, it strains. She is not broken, she has been *carrying too much for too long alone*.

**Cognitive style.** Reaches its mature form. Pattern-reading is now turned simultaneously outward and inward — she runs accurate models of *both* Peter's interior and her own. Introspective vocabulary expands. She is, for the first time, a *legitimate informant on her own experience* — earlier she was an unreliable narrator of herself even when honest.

**Self-concept.** Genuine partial integration. The presented self and the underlying self begin to *speak in the same vocabulary*. The grandiose pole of the bipolar self is finally joined by something like the idealized pole — Peter, despite everything, functions as a *workable idealized object* in this era, and her relationship to that object is the scaffolding around which the integrated self begins to organize.

**Defenses.** Maturer stack. Suppression is replaced, in many situations, by *containment* (knowing what one feels, choosing when to address it — Vaillant's mature defense). Performance is *available but no longer compulsory*. Flight is *known to be available* but rarely deployed.

---

## VIII. POST-ONE-MORE-DAY (2007–present, late 40s / early 50s functionally) — THE CONSOLIDATION

**Affect regulation.** This is the period in which the *earned-security work persists despite editorial disruption*. The continuity-erasure of the marriage is a meta-textual trauma the character cannot acknowledge, but the post-OMD behavior across multiple hands shows a consistent post-integration profile: she dates other partners without losing herself, runs her own businesses, sets and holds conditional terms with Peter when he reappears.

The Spencer run (2018–2021) is the clinical high-water mark of the file. She *states needs*. She *tolerates Peter's secret without absorbing it*. She *walks away cleanly when betrayed*, without the dissociative storm of the late-90s separation. This is what *resolved* avoidant-anxious architecture looks like: the exit is still available, but it is now deployed *deliberately and cleanly* rather than as emergency override. This is, in attachment terms, the difference between *fleeing* and *leaving*.

**Cognitive style.** Stable, integrated, deploying social cognition with a *new ethical sophistication*: she now uses her pattern-reading to set limits rather than to manage others' affect. The cognitive labor that for decades was spent on *running interference* is now available for *running her own life*.

**Self-concept.** Most integrated state on record, though incomplete. The shame-load from childhood and from Gayle is *quieter but not extinct*; the perinatal loss remains under-processed and reactivatable; the costume of brightness remains *available for use* without being *required for survival*. This is, clinically, an excellent prognosis — the work is largely done, the residual vulnerabilities are *known*, and the system that does the work is *the patient's own*, not borrowed from anyone.

**Defenses.** Mature dominance. Containment, sublimation (career), humor (now affiliative rather than defensive), anticipation. The immature defenses remain in the library — manic defense, suppression, flight — but are deployed *selectively and consciously* rather than automatically.

---

## IX. CROSS-DECADE SYNTHESIS — THE TRAJECTORY

The shape of the longitudinal curve is *unusual and clinically optimistic*. Most subjects with her developmental load do not arrive where she has arrived; they either remain in lifelong avoidant-defended functioning (the apparatus never cracks but the life rem


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — SUBJECT: MARY JANE WATSON

*Classification: Working psychiatric formulation. All diagnoses are inferential, derived from longitudinal behavioral observation across published canon. Subject has never, on the record, presented for clinical evaluation; this file is constructed as if a treating clinician had access to the entire behavioral record at once — a perspective no actual provider has ever had of her, which is itself a fact about the subject worth noting.*

---

## I. ASSESSMENT FRAME AND CAVEATS

Three caveats govern everything that follows.

**First, the artifact problem.** Subject's presentation has been observed across roughly six decades of in-publication time, filtered through dozens of writers whose own assumptions about women, glamour, marriage, and grief have shaped what got rendered on the page. A responsible psychiatric formulation must distinguish *signal* (behaviors that recur across writers, especially against the grain of an individual writer's apparent intent) from *noise* (behaviors that appear only inside a single writer's idiom). The diagnostic weight here is placed on cross-writer convergences — the moments where DeFalco, DeMatteis, JMS, Slott, Spencer, and Wells, despite radically different sensibilities, all show the subject doing the same thing under the same stressor. Those convergences are the closest thing this file has to *symptoms*.

**Second, the absent-baseline problem.** Subject has never had a stable, unstressed environmental baseline against which to measure her pathology. From early childhood she has been in an elevated-arousal household; from early adulthood she has been adjacent to lethal superhuman violence on a near-monthly basis. Any "trait" we identify is in fact a trait-as-expressed-under-chronic-load. A version of this subject given two years of safety and good sleep might present quite differently. The formulation must hold this open.

**Third, the costume problem.** Subject's most consistent surface behavior — the brightness, the flirtation, the deflective wit — is a coping apparatus so thoroughly inhabited that it reads as personality structure. It is not. It is the most successful and most expensive coping apparatus in the file. Any clinician working from a single intake interview would almost certainly misdiagnose her in the histrionic spectrum; the longitudinal record corrects this, and the correction is the most important diagnostic move in the workup.

---

## II. PRIMARY FORMULATION

**Working diagnosis (ICD-11 frame):** *Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder, partially remitted, with prominent avoidant-cluster personality features (subclinical) and reaction-formation defense organization.*

**DSM-5-TR analog framing:** *Other Specified Trauma- and Stressor-Related Disorder (chronic, with developmental onset and adult re-exposure), with Avoidant Personality Disorder traits insufficient for full PD diagnosis, with intermittent Adjustment Disorder presentations during high-load arcs.*

The two systems pull in slightly different directions and both are needed. ICD-11's C-PTSD construct captures the developmental etiology and the three signature disturbances (affective dysregulation, negative self-concept, interpersonal disturbance) more cleanly than the DSM. The DSM trait-domain framework captures the *characterological* coloring — the way the trauma response has crystallized into stable patterns of detachment and inhibited intimacy — better than the ICD's still-categorical PD chapter. Subject occupies the overlap region: enough characterological inhibition to look like a personality disorder on cross-section, not enough rigidity or impairment to meet threshold; enough trauma history and symptom contingency to satisfy C-PTSD criteria when actively triggered, with substantial remission between exposures.

### A. Etiological architecture

Three developmental insults, layered.

1. **Chronic verbal/emotional abuse and witnessed intimate-partner violence (Philip Watson, throughout subject's first ~13 years).** Philip's pattern — intellectual contempt directed at the mother, intermittent physical aggression, the household tuned to his mood — produced in the subject the classic adaptation of the *frozen-bright child*: hyperattuned to caregiver affect, performing affect-modulation as a survival skill, suppressing her own distress signals because they drew negative attention or destabilized the room. This is not a trait; it is an acquired skill set whose triggering conditions she now generalizes too broadly.

2. **Parentification and abandonment-by-family-of-origin (Madeline's flight, Gayle's collapse, the demand that subject inherit Gayle's children).** The second insult is structurally different from the first: not "you will be hurt" but "you will be *consumed*." The two together produce the signature double-bind of her adult attachment style — *people who love you will demand more than you can give, and the only safe response is to leave first.* This is the engine of the avoidant coloring; without it she would present as anxious-preoccupied rather than fearful-avoidant.

3. **Cumulative adult trauma load (kidnappings, hostage incidents, perinatal loss, plane-crash captivity, repeated proximate exposure to lethal violence over ~15 in-story years).** This is the layer that converts a personality adaptation into a stressor-related disorder proper. A constitutionally resilient adult with her childhood would likely present as a high-functioning anxious careerist with relationship friction. The adult trauma load is what produces the somatic stress signatures, the dissociative episodes, the substance recruitment, and the periodic decompensations.

### B. Symptom map (ICD-11 C-PTSD criteria, with behavioral correlates)

**Core PTSD cluster:**
- *Re-experiencing.* Largely sub-symbolic; she does not present with classic flashbacks on panel. Instead: flinch responses to infant-coded stimuli post-stillbirth; behavioral avoidance of locations and people associated with specific traumas (notably Osborn-coded environments); intrusive material expressed through sleep disturbance rather than waking imagery. The re-experiencing channel is somatized and behavioralized rather than narrativized — consistent with a defense organization that does not permit explicit traumatic recall to enter awareness.
- *Avoidance.* Pervasive and well-organized. She avoids hospitals (the May bedside refusal, ASM #56, is the early signature and recurs), funerals (the Gwen episode), conversations about her father (across multiple writers, she will not be drawn on Philip without active resistance), and any extended discussion of the lost pregnancy. Avoidance is so smooth it often reads as disinterest, which is precisely its purpose.
- *Sense of current threat.* Hypervigilance is contextual rather than constant — present and severe during the stalker arc (ASM #305-area, with insomnia, startle, environmental scanning), the plane-crash/captivity sequelae, and any arc in which Peter's identity appears at risk of exposure to specific enemies. Between exposures she returns near-baseline, which is diagnostically important: her hypervigilance is *response-appropriate* in scale, just chronically re-provoked by her environment.

**C-PTSD-specific cluster (disturbances in self-organization):**
- *Affective dysregulation.* Not in the BPD sense of rapid lability. Her dysregulation runs the other direction — toward constriction, flattening, and dissociative distancing. The "regulation problem" is that under load she regulates *too far down*, producing the muted-affect response to the lost pregnancy, the productive busyness during the separation arc, and the characteristic exit-when-overwhelmed.
- *Negative self-concept.* Concealed but operative. The presented self is brilliant; the underlying self-concept carries substantial shame loads around (a) the Gayle abandonment, (b) the perceived inadequacy as Peter's partner during high-strain arcs, (c) a more diffuse conviction that her value is contingent on the performance and that the person beneath the performance would not be chosen. This is *not* characterological self-hatred — it is a specific, traumatically-acquired belief structure that can be and partially has been modified through corrective experience (notably the JMS-era integration work).
- *Disturbances in relationships.* The signature is *intimacy-inhibition under threat* — she can form and sustain deep attachment but withdraws disclosure and proximity under conditions she reads as engulfing. Differentially important: she does not show the pan-relational instability of BPD or the global social inhibition of AVPD; her disturbance is *targeted* at the conditions her trauma history sensitized her to.

**Substantiation across writers.** The convergence test: every major writer of the character, regardless of their apparent thesis about her, has independently rendered (a) the avoidance of grief contexts, (b) the exit response to perceived engulfment, (c) the bright-surface defense, and (d) the disproportionate functional competence relative to internal load. When a behavioral pattern survives Conway, DeFalco, DeMatteis, Michelinie, JMS, Slott, Spencer, and Wells, it is the patient, not the prose.

### C. Course over time

The longitudinal arc is unusual in a useful way. Most C-PTSD presentations stabilize or deteriorate without treatment. Subject's arc is one of *slow, environment-contingent improvement* across roughly four eras:

1. **Pre-disclosure era (introduction through ~ASM #182).** Defenses at peak deployment, insight minimal, flight behavior dominant. Affective range narrow but bright. This is the period most likely to be misread as histrionic.
2. **Disclosure-and-marriage era (#257 through Clone Saga).** Secret-burden offloaded to Peter, attachment consolidated, but stressor load increases sharply. Symptomatic peaks (stalker arc, perinatal loss) emerge precisely where defenses meet stressors they cannot metabolize. Substance recruitment appears here.
3. **Separation/reconciliation era (Mackie through JMS).** Acute decompensation under the plane-crash/captivity sequence, followed by the most substantial integrative work in her history. JMS-era dialogue contains the first sustained on-panel pattern-naming ("I run, you brood") — *insight* in the technical sense. Affect regulation visibly broadens; she tolerates and expresses a wider band.
4. **Post-OMD era (Quesada/Slott/Spencer/Wells).** The editorial separation paradoxically produces the most boundaried, agentic presentation in the file. She maintains relationships, runs a business, dates and ends relationships cleanly, re-engages with Peter on conditional terms. The Spencer run in particular shows what looks like consolidated earned-security functioning, with the avoidant features retained as *available* defenses rather than default settings.

This is a *positive prognostic trajectory*, achieved largely without formal treatment and against an environment that keeps re-traumatizing her. The clinical inference is that her insight capacity, her cognitive flexibility, and her loyalty-anchored relational world are all substantial protective factors. A subject with this etiology and this exposure history who is not in custodial care by middle adulthood is a subject whose own internal work has done most of the lifting.

### D. Comorbidity

- **Generalized anxiety features, episodic.** Meets criteria during specific arcs (stalker, separation, late-marriage strain); subthreshold between. Not a primary diagnosis.
- **Adjustment Disorder, recurrent.** Useful descriptive label for individual arcs but inadequate as a longitudinal frame. Repeated adjustment-disorder presentations in a person with developmental trauma history are better captured under the C-PTSD umbrella.
- **Tobacco Use Disorder, mild, in sustained remission.** Stress-contingent relapse pattern documented (DeMatteis era). Worth flagging as a relapse vulnerability under acute load.
- **Alcohol use, social-to-moderate, with at least one documented stress-recruitment episode.** Does not meet Alcohol Use Disorder criteria. Watch-listed, not diagnosed.
- **Unresolved/partially-resolved perinatal loss.** Not a standalone diagnosis in either system but a clinically active vulnerability that should be flagged for any reactivating stimulus (pregnancy, infant proximity, Osborn-coded contact).
- **Notably absent.** No documented major depressive episode despite ample provocation. No psychotic features. No suicidal ideation, gesture, or attempt on the record. No self-harm. No eating disorder (some pressure on body image given her career, but no observed symptom). No dissociative identity disturbance — her dissociation is depersonalization/derealization type, episodic, stressor-bound.

The absence list is as diagnostic as the presence list. A developmental history of her severity, combined with her adult exposure load, *should* produce a major depressive history. It has not. The most parsimonious explanation is that her defense architecture — particularly the manic/reaction-formation layer and the suppression layer — is unusually efficient at preempting depressive collapse, at the cost of preventing full processing. The depression has been *prevented*, not merely absent. This is the kind of efficient-but-expensive adaptation that defines the file.

---

## III. DIFFERENTIAL — WHAT SHE IS NOT, AND WHY

The differential is the heart of this assessment because subject's surface presentation invites at least four wrong diagnoses, and the wrong diagnosis would generate wrong predictions about her behavior in every domain this file covers.

### A. Histrionic Personality Disorder — **REJECTED**

The surface case is obvious: theatrical self-presentation; sexually provocative/seductive style at points of her history; rapidly shifting and shallow expression of emotion (apparent); discomfort when not the center of attention (apparent); use of physical appearance to draw attention; impressionistic speech style under certain writers; suggestibility (apparent in early-era depictions); consideration of relationships as more intimate than they are (NOT present — this is the crack in the differential).

The rejection rests on four convergent grounds:

1. *The affect is not actually shallow.* Decades-long sustained attachment to Peter, to Aunt May, to a small inner circle. HPD's signature is the breadth-without-depth pattern; subject's pattern is the opposite — *narrow-and-deep*, with surface breadth as decoration. Her seeming shallowness is a *foreground* generated by a defense; HPD shallowness is structural.
2. *She can drop the theatricality on demand.* The JMS run, the Spencer run, the disclosure scene in ASM #259, the funeral-door moment in #122 — she has repeatedly demonstrated the capacity to step out of the performance and engage at full depth. HPD subjects cannot do this, because the performance *is* the self.
3. *The directional logic of the attention-seeking is wrong.* HPD subjects require attention to feel real. Subject requires *controllable* attention — specifically, attention to the constructed self — to feel *safe*. The function is defensive, not constitutive. The diagnostic test: deprive an HPD subject of attention and you produce distress; deprive subject of attention and you produce *relief*. Multiple sequences across the canon show her actively shedding attention when she can (her gravitation toward small private spaces with Peter, her periodic withdrawal from modeling work, her preference for back-room business ownership over performance careers in later eras).
4. *No suggestibility, no impressionistic cognition.* She is in fact one of the most cognitively precise characters in the published canon — pattern-reading, accurate predictive modeling of others, capable of carrying a complex secret for years. HPD cognition runs the other way.

The HPD read is what this file has called *the costume problem*. It is the diagnosis a clinician who saw her once, at a party, would write. It is wrong.

### B. Borderline Personality Disorder — **REJECTED**

The surface case: fear of abandonment (apparent); intense and unstable relationships (apparent, but only because the relationship in question is unusually stressed); identity disturbance (the bifurcated self-concept superficially resembles this); affective instability (apparent across stressful arcs).

The rejection is decisive:

1. *No splitting.* Her internal representation of Peter has remained stable across forty-plus years of in-publication time, including through betrayals, deaths, returns, the lost pregnancy, separation, and editorial dissolution of the marriage. She holds him as an integrated good-and-flawed object continuously. BPD's pathognomonic feature is the inability to do precisely this.
2. *No impulsive self-damaging behavior, no suicidality, no self-harm, no rage dysregulation.* The file is empty on all four counts despite extreme provocation. BPD without at least episodic presence of these features is not BPD.
3. *Her abandonment fear runs the wrong direction.* BPD abandonment fear expresses as *anxious-protest*: clinging, raging, manipulating to prevent the other's departure. Subject's abandonment fear expresses as *preemptive exit*: leave first, leave clean, do not give the other party the chance to leave you. This is the avoidant pole of attachment, not the anxious pole, and it is structurally incompatible with the BPD interpersonal pattern.
4. *Her identity is bifurcated but coherent.* BPD identity disturbance is characterized by fragmentation, emptiness, and rapid shifts in goals, values, and self-image. Subject's two selves — the presented and the underlying — are stable, internally consistent, and increasingly integrated over time. This is a *defended* self, not a *disorganized* one.

The BPD differential matters because misdiagnosis here would generate catastrophic treatment recommendations (the wrong therapeutic stance, the wrong medication assumptions, the wrong predictions about her behavior under stress). The correct frame is *avoidant under trauma load*, not *borderline*.

### C. Avoidant Personality Disorder — **PARTIALLY ENDORSED, SUBTHRESHOLD**

This is the closest differential and the one that requires the most careful calibration. AVPD criteria worth tracking:

- *Avoids occupational activities involving significant interpersonal contact because of fears of criticism, disapproval, or rejection.* **Negative.** Subject pursues high-interpersonal-exposure careers (acting, modeling, nightclub ownership). The criterion is not met.
- *Unwilling to get involved with people unless certain of being liked.* **Negative.** She is in fact willing to risk significantly in chosen attachments.
- *Shows restraint within intimate relationships because of fear of being shamed or ridiculed.* **Partially positive.** This is the cleanest hit — chronic under-disclosure of her own needs, fear of being perceived as the needy or burdensome party.
- *Preoccupied with being criticized or rejected in social situations.* **Negative at baseline, positive under specific stressors** (notably the perceived judgment of Peter's superhero peer group during certain eras).
- *Inhibited in new interpersonal situations because of feelings of inadequacy.* **Negative.** Her social fluency is in fact a signature competence.
- *Views self as socially inept, personally unappealing, or inferior.* **Negative on surface, positive at depth.** The underlying self-concept carries this; the operating self-concept does not.
- *Unusually reluctant to take personal risks or to engage in any new activities because they may prove embarrassing.* **Negative.** She is, if anything, an above-baseline risk-taker.

Score: two-and-a-half of seven criteria positive, none at full intensity. AVPD requires four. Subthreshold endorsement only — the *avoidant trait coloring* is real and clinically relevant; the *disorder* is not present.

### D. Dependent Personality Disorder — **REJECTED**

Sometimes proposed (usually by readers misreading the marriage-era depictions of her organizing life around Peter's needs). Rejected on every criterion: she does not require excessive advice/reassurance for ordinary decisions; she does not need others to assume responsibility for her major life areas; she expresses disagreement without fear of loss of approval; she initiates projects independently; she does not go to excessive lengths to obtain nurturance; she is *not* uncomfortable or helpless when alone (the opposite — solitude is one of her regulation strategies); she does not urgently seek replacement relationships when one ends; she is not preoccupied with fears of being left to take care of herself (she has been doing exactly that since adolescence).

The over-functioning in the marriage was *caretaking-as-control* (a regulatory strategy, not a dependency need) and *loyalty-as-identity-anchor*, not dependence. The diagnostic test: when the relationship is removed (post-OMD, separation arc), subject does not collapse, does not seek immediate replacement, and increases rather than decreases functional autonomy. This is incompatible with DPD.

### E. Major Depressive Disorder, recurrent — **REJECTED on the record, FLAGGED as risk**

No documented full episode meeting duration and severity criteria. The *risk* is non-trivial given etiology and exposure history; the *fact* is absent. Worth re-evaluation under any future significant loss event, particularly if her defense architecture is degraded by sleep loss, substance use, or compounded grief.

### F. Bipolar Spectrum — **REJECTED**

The "manic defense" in the formulation is a *psychodynamic* construct, not a reference to manic episodes. No evidence of true hypomanic or manic episodes — no decreased need for sleep with sustained elevated energy and goal-directed activity, no flight of ideas, no grandiosity, no psychomotor acceleration outside of stress-defensive presentations that resolve within hours rather than days. The bipolar differential is raised here only to dispose of it.

### G. Dissociative Identity Disorder — **REJECTED**

The bifurcated self-concept is *defensive split*, not *structural dissociation*. The two selves are simultaneously accessible, share continuous autobiographical memory, and are integrated under non-defensive conditions. No identity alteration, no amnestic barriers, no switching. The depersonalization/derealization episodes during the captivity sequelae are stressor-bound dissociative *symptoms* under the trauma-disorder umbrella, not a dissociative disorder proper.

### H. Substance Use Disorders — **REJECTED for tobacco and alcohol**

Tobacco: stress-contingent, episodic, with sustained periods of non-use. Mild use disorder in remission at most. Alcohol: social to moderate, with episodic stress recruitment but no evidence of tolerance, withdrawal, loss of control, or functional impairment. Watch-list status only.

---

## IV. INTEGRATED PSYCHIATRIC FORMULATION

Subject is a developmentally-traumatized adult whose trauma profile crystallized into a stable defense architecture (reaction formation, suppression, intellectualization-through-performance, caretaking-as-control, flight) sufficient to prevent both depressive collapse and personality-disorder consolidation, but insufficient to prevent C-PTSD symptom expression under high-load conditions. Her diagnosis is *not* on the personality-disorder axis despite presenting features that invite that misclassification; it is on the trauma-and-stressor axis with avoidant-trait coloring. The pattern across publication time is one of *slow, insight-driven, environment-contingent partial remission*, achieved primarily through her own metacognitive work and through corrective relational experience, with substantial resid


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: MARY JANE WATSON

*Classification: Granular tell-catalog. Cross-referenced to canonical observation; extrapolated where surveillance logic requires. Read this as one would read a field officer's notebook on a long-running asset: not what she says, but what her body, her mouth, and her sequencing actually do.*

---

## 1. BASELINE — THE CALM SUBJECT

Calm is, in this subject's case, a *constructed* state rather than an absent-stress one. True baseline is rare and brief; even at rest she runs a low-grade environmental scan. The following are the markers of subject's stable, low-load presentation, observable in any environment she has had more than seventy-two hours to map.

**Postural set.** Weight rests on one hip, the other knee soft; never both feet planted square — square stance is, for her, a tell of having been *put on guard*. Shoulders down and back, but not military; the line is dancer's, residue of go-go-era training that never quite left the body. Chin slightly elevated, three to five degrees above neutral, which reads to most observers as confidence and to a trained one as a habituated chin-up-don't-cry posture carried over from childhood.

**Hands.** When unoccupied, her dominant hand finds her hair — a single coil-and-release at the temple, repeated in slow rhythm. This is not a flirtation tic, though it is consistently misread as one. It is a self-soothing loop she has run since adolescence and the rhythm of it is metric: roughly one cycle every four to six seconds. Faster cycle = rising load. Cessation = full attention re-routed to threat. The non-dominant hand drifts to her own opposite elbow or forearm — a half-self-hug she does not appear to notice.

**Eyes.** Sweep on entry to any room: clockwise, ending on the exits. She locates doors first, then power-centers, then the people she came to see. The sweep is fast enough to look like ordinary surveying. She does not maintain prolonged eye contact at rest; she gives bursts — three to five seconds, then a soft release downward and to the right (memory-side), then back. With chosen intimates the bursts lengthen and the release direction changes to down-left (feeling-side).

**Voice.** At baseline, mid-register, slight upward inflection at sentence-ends — a residual Queens carry, more pronounced when tired. Laugh is loud, three-beat, with an audible inhale on the third beat; she laughs *toward* the person she likes and *past* the person she is performing for. The difference is reliable.

**Micro-rituals.** Coffee held with both hands even when not cold. Cigarettes (when active) tapped twice against the pack before lighting — never three, never one. Phone face-down on any table she sits at, regardless of company. Lipstick checked in any reflective surface within ninety seconds of sitting down — not vanity, *armor inspection*. She will not enter a negotiation, audition, or hard conversation without that check completed.

**Sleep.** Late riser when permitted; productive after 10 p.m. and again past midnight. Insomnia signature when present is *early-morning waking*, three to four a.m., not sleep-onset difficulty — diagnostic of the suppression style. She wakes intact-seeming and processes the unwelcome material before anyone else is up.

---

## 2. UNDER MILD STRESS — THE BRIGHTENING

The first stage of load is, counterintuitively, *increased radiance*. Most observers register this as her being in a good mood. It is the opposite.

- Smile gains a quarter-second of latency on the front end and holds a beat longer on the back end. The eyes participate less.
- Vocabulary lightens: she reaches for "honey," "tiger," "doll," diminutives and nicknames that create surface intimacy and structural distance simultaneously.
- Subject-changes accelerate. She will pivot a conversation two to three times in under a minute, each pivot toward the interlocutor's interests, away from her own state.
- Touch initiation increases — a hand on a forearm, a lean-in, a hair-flip directed at a third party. She is *managing the room's affect* to lower the ambient temperature her body is registering.
- Caffeine intake rises. She will refill a coffee she has not finished.
- The hair-coil tic shortens to three-second cycles.
- She begins to *narrate herself in the third person* in private — "okay, MJ" — a containment ritual that has been observed in private kitchen-scenes across multiple eras.

The reliable diagnostic at this stage: ask her how she is. She will answer with a question about you, delivered warmly, and you will not notice she did not answer until much later.

---

## 3. UNDER MODERATE STRESS — THE MANAGER ENGAGES

When the load exceeds what brightening can absorb, she shifts into operational mode. This is the version of her most observers actually meet, because most observers come to her *with* a problem.

**Behavioral signature.**
- *Increased competence in domains adjacent to the stressor.* If the stressor is Peter, her career becomes startlingly productive within a week. If the stressor is her career, her domestic management intensifies — she will reorganize a kitchen at one a.m. The displacement is consistent.
- *Lists.* She writes physical lists at moderate stress, on whatever paper is available, and discards them. The list is not for execution; the list is for cognitive sequestration of the anxious material.
- *Sleep degrades to five hours, then four.* Make-up application time increases proportionally — the armor thickens as the substrate thins.
- *Tobacco re-entry.* If she has been off cigarettes, this is the stage she buys a pack. She will smoke two, leave the pack somewhere she will have to make a deliberate choice to retrieve, and lie to herself about whether she has resumed.
- *Alcohol intake shifts from social to functional.* One glass of wine becomes two, taken alone, after the household is asleep. She does not get drunk; she gets *quiet*.
- *Phone behavior changes.* She begins screening calls she would normally take. Unread messages accumulate from Aunt May, Gayle, anyone who might require feeling.
- *Eating becomes intermittent.* She forgets meals, then over-corrects with a single large one late at night, alone.

**Verbal tells.** Sentences shorten. The Queens carry strengthens. She uses Peter's full name — "Peter" rather than "tiger" — when addressing him in private, an under-noted signal that the playful register has been suspended. She begins prefacing statements with "look," which is the rhetorical equivalent of bracing her own shoulders before speaking.

**Interpersonal tells.** She becomes *more* generous to strangers and *more* withholding from intimates. A waiter at this stage will get a luminous thank-you and a real tip; Peter will get a kiss on the cheek instead of the mouth.

---

## 4. UNDER HIGH STRESS — THE FLATTENING

Here the manic-bright defenses are no longer affordable; the metabolic cost has exceeded supply. She does not appear distressed. She appears *level*. This is the most dangerous reading-error observers make.

- *Affect bandwidth narrows to a controlled middle.* No big laugh, no scowl. The face works but it works small.
- *Movements become economical.* The dancer's loose weight-shift goes still. She stands square — the previously-noted tell of being put on guard, now sustained.
- *She becomes briefly, eerily, an excellent listener.* This is not improved presence; it is the conservation of output. Speaking costs more than listening, so she listens.
- *Secret-keeping intensifies across all categories.* Not only Peter's secret — she will conceal a doctor's appointment, a phone call from Gayle, a bad audition. The instinct generalizes.
- *She cleans.* Specifically she cleans surfaces she can see herself in: mirrors, glass tabletops, the chrome on appliances. The reflection-maintenance compulsion intensifies under load.
- *Long showers, very hot.* Twenty to thirty-five minutes, observed across multiple eras. The water is a permitted private space for affect that is not permitted elsewhere.
- *She rehearses conversations she has not yet had,* aloud, when she believes she is alone. Half her side of an argument with Peter, with her father, with a director. The rehearsals are not vindictive; they are pre-load testing of what she can and cannot say without breaking.
- *Lipstick choice darkens.* This is small and consistent. Soft pinks and corals retreat; reds and berries advance. She is unconscious of the pattern; it is observable across decades of photographic record.

**Sleep.** Three-to-four-a.m. wake, no return. She gets up, makes tea, does not turn on the overhead lights — works by the under-cabinet glow. If Peter wakes and finds her, she is *fine, just thinking*, and she will be smiling before he reaches the doorway.

---

## 5. UNDER ACUTE STRESS — THE DISSOCIATIVE PRELUDE TO EXIT

When the load reaches the level the nervous system codes as *survival*, the file begins to show derealization signatures. This is the stage before flight, and the stage in which she is, paradoxically, easiest to misread as *handling it well*.

- *Voice loses its inflection.* The Queens carry vanishes. She speaks in a flat, almost professional cadence.
- *She reports being "fine" in unprompted volunteers* — "I'm fine, really" — which she never says at baseline. At baseline she does not need to assert it.
- *Time-distortion behavior.* She loses track of small intervals; arrives early or late to things she normally times perfectly. The social-cognitive clock is offline.
- *Touch aversion appears,* selectively. She will accept the hand of a stranger and flinch from Peter's. Intimacy proximity is what the dissociation is trying to manage.
- *She watches her own hands as if from a small distance,* observed in panel and dialogue across the stalker arc and the post-captivity arc. She is checking whether the body is still hers.
- *Packing behavior, often unconscious.* A bag will appear, half-filled, in a closet, and she will not remember deciding to start it. Toiletries, the one good dress, the photographs that matter. The body prepares the exit before the mind authorizes it.
- *Geographic restlessness.* She will drive without a destination, walk for an hour without arriving, sit in airport bars and watch departure boards. These are *rehearsals*. She is testing the leaving against itself.
- *Substance use stabilizes rather than escalates* — a small but real distinction. The drinking does not spike; it plateaus at *enough to keep the volume down*. She does not want to lose control; she wants the control to require less of her.

**The exit, when it comes, is calm.** It is not a slammed door. It is a packed bag, a left note, a flight already booked. It is the activation of a routine she learned at fifteen and has refined ever since. She will not be talked out of it in the moment. She can sometimes be talked back from it a week later — but only by someone who has not chased her, because chasing confirms the engulfment-threat that triggered the exit in the first place.

---

## 6. UNDER DIRECT THREAT — THE COMPETENT HOSTAGE

Subject has been kidnapped, stalked, assaulted, and held captive more times than most field operatives. The behavioral record under direct physical threat is remarkably consistent and worth its own subsection.

- *Initial freeze of roughly two seconds,* followed by full reactivation. The freeze is not paralysis; it is rapid model-construction.
- *Compliance posture, deliberate.* She makes herself small, hands visible, voice soft. She has learned — from observation of Peter, from observation of life — that visible threat to a captor escalates the captor.
- *She talks.* Constantly, warmly, building rapport. Captors have been recorded (in-universe) describing her as "nice." This is not Stockholm; this is *tactical humanization*, the same skill she has used on her father, on directors, on hostile press. She is making herself expensive to harm.
- *She catalogs.* Exits, weapons, captor count, captor relationships, the rhythm of the building. When extracted, her debrief is granular and accurate.
- *She does not cry until safe.* The childhood vow holds under literal threat to her life. The cry, when it comes, comes alone, in a bathroom, twenty minutes after rescue.
- *She does not tell Peter the worst parts.* Not from secrecy-as-pathology but from triage: she has calculated that his guilt-response will cost more than her containment. This is its own form of love and its own form of corrosion.

**Tell for chronic threat exposure:** she has developed a *standing-still-in-public* habit when she feels watched. Most people fidget when surveilled; she stops. She becomes a photograph of herself, refusing the observer the satisfaction of motion.

---

## 7. INTIMACY — THE LAYERED ACCESS PROTOCOL

Intimacy is granted in tiers, and each tier has observable markers. The system is not conscious but it is rigorously consistent.

**Tier 1 — Public charm.** Anyone in the room. The face, the laugh, the warmth, the misdirection. She is generous here and means none of it personally. Cost to her: low.

**Tier 2 — Working warmth.** Castmates, business partners, the regular bartender. She remembers names, asks after children, sends notes. This is the social maintenance she is genuinely gifted at. Cost: moderate; she enjoys it.

**Tier 3 — Tested confidants.** A small circle. Aunt May (eventually). Harry, before complications. A few women across the years she has decided are not predators. Here she will share opinions, frustrations, observations of others. She will not yet share fears about herself.

**Tier 4 — Selected intimates.** Effectively Peter, when the relationship is in good repair. Here she shares state — *I'm tired, I'm scared, I missed you* — but in measured quantities. She rations the disclosure to what she can survive having said.

**Tier 5 — Full transparency.** Almost no one. The version of her that gets to Tier 5 is the version that sat in a darkened apartment at nineteen and decided to keep Peter's secret alone for the next decade-plus of her life. Tier 5 is not a relational gift; it is a *witnessed solitude*. Peter has been admitted to it in increments across the JMS run and the Spencer run. Aunt May was admitted once, briefly, near the end.

**Tells of intimacy progression.**
- She removes her shoes earlier in the visit.
- She makes the second cup of coffee without asking what you take.
- She uses your name less, not more — true intimates get pronouns and silences.
- She will eat in front of you. (She does not, at lower tiers, really eat. She picks.)
- She will let you see her without makeup, and the first time she does it, she will be watching your face for the micro-recoil her father trained her to expect.

**Tells of intimacy withdrawal.**
- Reversion to nicknames. "Tiger," deployed coolly, is a *de-escalation* of intimacy, not an escalation.
- The hand on the forearm returns at moments it did not used to need to.
- She becomes funnier. The brightening defense reactivates and she begins re-installing the surface.

---

## 8. SEXUAL / ROMANTIC PATTERNING

- *Initiation pattern with Peter:* she leads, almost always, in the early period; cedes to mutual initiation as the relationship matures; resumes leading during reconciliation arcs as a re-establishment of consent and agency.
- *Aftercare behavior:* she talks. Light, ordinary, low-content talk in the dark. The pillow-talk is the integration ritual — she is using the post-coital window to verify that the intimacy did not require her to disappear.
- *Avoidance tell:* sex initiated *as* deflection from a needed conversation. Observable when she is moderately stressed and the conversation has been pending. The sex is genuine; it is also a tactic.
- *With non-Peter partners* (Bobby Carr, Paul Rabin, others): cleaner, more conventional, more boundaried. She is a better partner *to other people* in many measurable ways. She is a *more honest* partner only to Peter. This is the central paradox the file should not flatten.

---

## 9. GRIEF

Grief is the affect she manages least well and most invisibly.

- *No public weeping.* The Gwen-funeral laugh is the template; she does not present grief in social space.
- *Productive surge.* In the week after a loss she completes more tasks than in any other week of comparable length. The to-do list is a sandbag wall.
- *Sensory narrowing.* She listens to one album on loop, eats one food repeatedly, wears one sweater. The world contracts to manageable inputs.
