**She will work jobs she finds distasteful** to maintain financial independence — soap opera roles she despises (Stern era), nightclub management with mob-adjacent investors (Slott), modeling assignments that traffic on the exact decorative-object reading of her that she most resents. The principle she enacts: *self-sufficiency outranks dignity-of-occupation*. This is a Depression-era ethic in a glamour-industry body.

---

## 7.3 What She Will Not Do

**She will not strike first.** No on-panel instance of her initiating violence. She has slapped people (Peter, once or twice; a paparazzo in the Slott era; her father in flashback) and the slaps are always responsive, always to a specific verbal-or-physical provocation, and always at the *lowest* viable force. She is not pacifist by conviction; she is non-aggressive by formation. Aggression was her father's vocabulary and she will not borrow it.

**She will not expose an identity.** Peter's, Felicia's, Harry's-as-Goblin in the arcs she knew. Even under duress. Even when angry. Even when it would clarify a public misunderstanding that costs her professionally. This is the strongest single line in her code.

**She will not weaponize a child.** Notable across the Renew Your Vows material and the alternate-future depictions: she will hide Annie, lie to Annie, protect Annie at extraordinary cost, but she will not place Annie in a position calculated to coerce Peter's behavior. The mere consideration of doing so, in one Conway sequence, registers on her face as nausea.

**She will not stay in a relationship organized around her decorative function.** The Bobby Carr arc terminates on exactly this trigger — the moment she perceives that she is functioning as accessory rather than partner, she goes. Same with the modeling agencies that try to shape her career around her face exclusively; she has fired representation more than once in the back-matter of issues where it doesn't even drive plot.

**She will not perform her own suffering for sympathy.** This is one of her most diagnostically interesting prohibitions. She will let Peter see her cry only when fully overwhelmed, and even then she frequently turns her face. She does not narrate her pain to friends. She does not, ever, use the perinatal loss as leverage in an argument despite the rhetorical power it would carry. The taboo is profound and self-imposed.

**She will not condescend.** Even to people who deserve it. Jameson, Flash Thompson in his early belligerent period, her father in the few panels of confrontation, Norman Osborn — her vocabulary toward each remains free of contempt. She will mock, she will sharpen, she will refuse, but she will not look down on. The discipline here is so consistent it must be understood as a vow.

**She will not become her sister.** Negative imperative, but operationally enormous. She will not collapse into a man's life as identity-substrate. She will not let circumstance dictate her aperture. She will not be the woman waiting to be rescued from her own choices. Every major career and relational decision can be read as enforcement of this prohibition.

**She will not become her father.** The corresponding negative imperative. She will not belittle. She will not envy publicly. She will not punish a partner for being better-loved by the world than she is. (Note: Peter is, in their universe, both celebrated and reviled; she has had ample provocation in both directions and has produced neither resentment nor possessive pride.)

---

## 7.4 Justifications (When She Bothers)

Subject rarely justifies her decisions verbally, and when she does, the justifications are notably *plain* — first-order, situation-specific, free of grand-theory. Sample register, distilled across writers:

- *"He needed someone to know."* (On the long secret-keeping, JMS run.)
- *"I'm not going to be the reason he stops."* (On not asking Peter to quit, multiple eras.)
- *"You don't get to talk to me like that."* (Boundary statements, post-OMD, particularly Spencer.)
- *"I'm not leaving you. I'm leaving this."* (Mackie separation; reprised in different language under Spencer.)
- *"It's my job."* (On hazardous protection of others, said with the affect of a working professional.)

The pattern: her ethics speak in declarative sentences about *this situation, this person, this line*. She does not generalize. Asked to articulate a principle, she will usually deflect into a joke. This is partly defensive — abstract moral language was her father's preferred weapon — and partly accurate self-knowledge: she *does* legislate case-by-case, and she does not wish to overclaim consistency she has not earned.

---

## 7.5 Where the Code is Consistent

Astonishingly, across nearly sixty years of publication and dozens of writers of variable quality, the code holds. The consistencies, ranked by robustness:

- **Loyalty to chosen intimates.** Zero defections on record. Every apparent defection (the #183 disappearance; the Mackie separation; the Spencer walk) is, on close reading, a defection from a *situation* rather than from the person.
- **Refusal to expose identity.** Zero breaches on record across all continuities including Ultimate, MC2, Renew Your Vows, and the post-OMD mainline.
- **Refusal of cruelty in departure.** Even her hardest exits are clean. No revenge phase. No public airing. No use of press access she demonstrably has.
- **Refusal to condescend.** Zero observed breaches. This may be the single most stable behavioral feature in her file.
- **Self-sufficiency imperative.** Across every era, she works. Even married to a man who would prefer she be safe and supported, she works.

---

## 7.6 Where the Code Fractures

Honest assessment requires noting the seams.

**Fracture 1 — Honesty with herself about why she is leaving.** When she exits, her stated reasons are usually true but not complete. The #183 refusal was framed as not wanting marriage; it was also flight from a man whose proximity to death triggered her oldest survival routine. The Mackie separation was framed as needing space; it was also a PTSD response she did not yet have language for. She does not lie to others about her reasons so much as *under-specify* them — and the under-specification protects her from having to examine the architecture beneath. The JMS era is the first sustained period in which she begins closing this gap.

**Fracture 2 — The Gayle debt.** She fled responsibility for her sister's children. By her own code (rule 5: protect the people too tired to protect themselves), this is a violation. She has never reconciled it. Her over-functioning for Aunt May, for Harry, for Peter, for civilians she does not know, reads in part as displaced restitution. The fracture is real, she knows it is real, and her ethics around children — including the perinatal loss, including her conduct toward Normie Osborn in the few scenes she has with him — carry the weight of an undischarged debt.

**Fracture 3 — Self-erasure inside the marriage.** During the Michelinie-through-Mackie era, her code's rule 2 (do not make another responsible for your survival) metastasized into rule 2-prime: *do not have needs visible enough to burden him*. This is a corruption of the original principle and she pays for it somatically (insomnia, smoking, eventual collapse). The post-OMD era is the documented correction. The fracture was real; the repair is observable.

**Fracture 4 — Charm-as-tool versus charm-as-deception.** Her line between instrumental charm (acceptable) and manipulative deception (not) is drawn by *intent and target*, not by *technique*. The technique is identical. An honest file notes that this line is partly self-serving — it permits her to do, in service of her own ends, things that would offend her if done to someone she loved. She is aware of this. The Spencer run has a beat where she catches herself running a charm-operation on Peter and stops, visibly, mid-sentence. The awareness is recent and incomplete.

**Fracture 5 — The "earned access" clause to honesty.** Rule 6 is operationally sound but creates a tier of people — most people — to whom she feels no obligation of truth. This is efficient and protective but it has costs: it means she goes through life with very few people who actually know her, and the loneliness it produces sometimes surfaces as the very flight-pressure her code is designed to manage. The rule, in other words, partly produces the stress it exists to mitigate.

**Fracture 6 — She will not perform her own suffering, and this prevents others from helping her.** The prohibition (7.3) is morally admirable and clinically costly. Held strictly, it makes her unreadable to people who would happily share her load. The JMS-era partial relaxation of this rule is the period of her highest observed wellbeing — direct evidence that the prohibition, while ethically intended, functions as self-harm.

---

## 7.7 Drift Over Time

The code itself has not changed. Its *application* has matured.

**Phase I — Pre-introduction through mid-Conway (childhood through ASM ~#180).** Code is reflexive, unexamined, primarily expressed as *avoid causing the kind of pain my father caused*. Rules are present but unintegrated. Lying is fluent; charm is reflexive; loyalty is intense but secret. The girl at Gwen's funeral has the code already but cannot yet meet what the code demands of her.

**Phase II — Return through pre-marriage (ASM #257-#290s).** Code articulated to herself for the first time during the #259 disclosure. The act of telling Peter her history is the first occasion on which her ethics become *speakable*. She begins to apply the code consciously: chooses to stay, chooses to disclose, chooses to be present at the wedding.

**Phase III — Marriage era (1987-1998).** Code holds at the level of loyalty, fractures at the level of self-care. She over-applies rule 2 and under-applies rule 5-to-self. Somatic and substance costs accumulate. The code is being used against its bearer.

**Phase IV — Separation and JMS reconciliation (1998-2007).** First real revision. She begins to add an unspoken rule 8: *I count among the people I am required to protect*. This rule is fragile, contested, and the work of integrating it is the through-line of her best-written years.

**Phase V — Post-OMD (2007-present).** Rule 8 hardens. Boundaries become declarative. The code is now spoken in full sentences when necessary ("you don't get to talk to me like that"; "I'm not doing this again"). Loyalty remains absolute; self-erasure is gone. This is the most integrated her ethics have ever been on the record, and the integration is hers — earned, not granted.

---

## 7.8 Comparative Note

The closest moral analogues in the canon are not the costumed figures and not the obvious civilian counterparts. She does not share Peter's responsibility-as-debt framework; she does not share May's faith-based forbearance; she does not share Felicia's transactional ethics. Her code most resembles, in structure and tone, the working ethics of long-tenured trauma workers — the ER nurse, the hostage negotiator's spouse, the war correspondent who has stopped being shocked. *Small number of rules. Held hard. Articulated reluctantly. Enforced without drama. Revised slowly and only under evidence.*

The genuinely apt historical comparison, offered carefully, is to the moral style of women who survived authoritarian households by becoming the family's interpreter — the daughters in Czesław Miłosz's or Vivian Gornick's accounts, who learned ethics in the negative, by cataloguing what the father did and refusing it, and who built quiet, durable, case-by-case codes that outlasted the regimes they were formed against. Subject's ethics are of that lineage. They are not glamorous. They are not systematic. They are, on the evidence of sixty years, **load-bearing** — and they have held weight that the more elaborated moral systems around her have, repeatedly, dropped.

*End Section 7. Proceed to Section 8 — Tradecraft, Habits, and Operational Routines.*


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — SUBJECT: MARY JANE WATSON

Classification: Longitudinal linguistic surveillance synthesis. Speech samples drawn from Lee/Romita introduction (ASM #42, 1966) through Wells run (present). Cross-referenced against alternate-continuity samples (Ultimate, Renew Your Vows, Spider-Girl flash-forwards) for stability of idiolect under different authorial hands.

---

## 1. BASELINE REGISTER — THE DEFAULT VOICE

Subject's default speaking voice is a mid-Atlantic American English overlaid with light residual Queens — the Queens surfaces only in two contexts: (a) emotional escalation, where dropped *g*'s and tightened vowels return ("nothin'," "talkin'," "ya kiddin' me"), and (b) deliberate code-switch downward when she wants to signal solidarity with a working-class interlocutor or undercut someone's pretension. Both are markers. The baseline she presents in neutral social settings is *acquired* — the speech of someone who consciously polished an accent to be castable, employable, and class-mobile. This is itself a linguistic tell: the standard register is the costume; the borough is the body underneath.

Speech rate is fast — measurably faster than Peter Parker's, faster than most of her female peer set in the canon. She talks *over* silences rather than into them. Pauses are managed: she will fill a beat with a small physical sound (laugh, exhale, a hummed *mm*) rather than allow dead air, because dead air is where the room can turn on her. The few instances on panel where she allows a long silence are diagnostic of either (a) full safety (late-arc Peter, Aunt May after the secret-share) or (b) total shutdown (separation arc, post-stillbirth).

Pitch travels higher in performance-mode (party scenes, public events, first encounters) and drops noticeably when she is alone with a trusted intimate — by the JMS run this drop is overt and Peter notices it on panel. The "real" voice is lower, slower, and approximately a third less verbose per beat than the public voice.

---

## 2. THE PARTY-GIRL REGISTER — INTRODUCTION-ERA AND ITS HALF-LIFE

The Lee/Romita-period voice is its own register and never fully retires; it gets recruited under specific conditions for the rest of her life. Markers:

- **Tiger.** The single most overdetermined word in the file. First deployed at introduction ("Face it, tiger — you just hit the jackpot"), it persists for sixty publication-years as a *targeted-affection signal* used exclusively for Peter. She does not call other men *tiger*. The word does three jobs at once: it claims him, it diminishes the threat-content of an emotional moment with mock-predator playfulness, and it preserves plausible deniability — *I'm not being sincere, I'm being cute*. When she uses *tiger* in a serious sentence, the seriousness is being smuggled. Track frequency: high in courtship, dips during marriage-routine, spikes around reconciliations and goodbyes. Its appearance in a goodbye is a near-certain marker that the goodbye is not final in her own internal model.
- **Daddy-O, Buster, Sport, Mister, Webhead, Web-head, Hot Stuff.** A rotating arsenal of mock-diminutives, period-coded to the 60s/70s in origin but kept alive into modern continuity as deliberate retro-cute affect. They are *all* deflection-vocatives: she nicknames people to manage them.
- **Italicized exclamations of delight** — "*Wow*," "*Crazy*," "*Wild*," "*Far out*" in early canon; updated to "*God*," "*Jesus*," "*Wow, okay*" later. The function is constant: she is performing surprise/pleasure at a volume designed to fill the room.
- **Self-third-person.** "MJ doesn't do mornings." "MJ needs coffee." Used sparingly, always under mild stress, always to put narrative distance between the speaking-self and the experiencing-self. A subtle but consistent dissociative-flag in the corpus.
- **The trailing laugh.** Sentences in this register frequently end on a soft laugh that is not synced to actual humor — a verbal *period* rather than an emotional response. The trailing laugh is the most reliable marker that she is operating in defensive-performance mode and not in earnest. Its *absence* in dialogue with Peter is the single fastest indicator that she has dropped the costume.

---

## 3. THE WORKING VOICE — CAREER, BUSINESS, MANAGEMENT

When subject is operating professionally — modeling sets, audition rooms, the nightclub-ownership arcs, Stark Industries adjacency (post-OMD), the rare reporter-mode in Ultimate continuity — her register tightens dramatically. Markers:

- Sentence length shortens. Verb-forward syntax. She gives instructions in two-beat units: *Move the light. Try it again.*
- Diminutives drop almost entirely; vocatives become functional (first names, *sir*, *honey* as light-professional-lubricant rather than affection).
- She uses the imperative more frequently than any other character in her social orbit. She is comfortable telling people what to do, and it does not register to her as aggression — it registers as efficiency. This is *not* the party girl. This is the daughter of Madeline Watson running the household at twelve.
- Negotiation language is clean, declarative, and unhedged. She does not pad refusals ("I'd love to, but —"); she refuses ("No, that doesn't work for me"). The lack of hedging in professional contexts is the single largest register-gap from her romantic-context speech, where hedging is endemic.
- Profanity light to moderate, deployed for emphasis, never for venting. *Damn*, *hell*, the occasional *shit* in modern canon. She does not use slurs, and she does not escalate to harder profanity even under acute professional stress — a marker of someone who has learned that women who curse hard at work get re-categorized.

---

## 4. THE SECRET-KEEPER REGISTER — WHAT SHE WITHHOLDS, AND HOW

The behavioral fact that subject carried Peter's secret for two in-story decades before disclosure (ASM #257) requires a specialized linguistic profile: this is a person *trained in active concealment within affectionate dialogue*. Her techniques:

- **Topic-redirection via affection.** When a line of conversation approaches a fact she must not surface, she does not change the subject — she *deepens the current one* with a more intimate beat that consumes the interlocutor's attention. Compliment, joke, light touch, fresh question about the other person. The redirect is so warm it does not register as a redirect.
- **Strategic incomplete sentences.** She trails off with "…anyway" or "…you know what I mean" at moments where completing the thought would expose knowledge she shouldn't have. Cross-reference her speech across the 70s pre-reveal: the incidence of mid-sentence trail-offs is significantly higher in Peter-adjacent dialogue than in any other context.
- **Questions she already knows the answer to.** Long-running pattern. Asking Peter *why he's late* when she has watched him swing out the window is not deception so much as protocol-maintenance — the giving of a script for him to perform safely. Post-disclosure, this pattern persists with new content (asking about injuries she has already triaged from across the room).
- **The asymmetric "I know."** When she finally does disclose knowledge, she does it in compact, low-affect sentences. "I know who you are. I've always known." The disclosure-syntax is short, even-stressed, and stripped of her usual ornament — *because the ornament is the lie, and removing it is the signal that this is true*. This pattern recurs at every major honesty-moment of her life. Watch for the *shortening of the line* as the marker of truth-telling.

---

## 5. HOW SHE COMMUNICATES LOVE

Subject's love-language is structurally indirect. She does not, on the record, deploy *I love you* casually. The phrase appears in her speech maybe a dozen times across decades of canon; each instance is high-stakes, often crisis-adjacent, and frequently followed by physical exit from the room. *I love you* is, for her, a sentence that costs.

Her *operational* love-language is denser and more reliable:

- **Naming.** She calls intimates by name more than the average speaker — *Peter*, *May*, in moments where a pronoun would suffice. The name is a touch.
- **The *tiger*-deployment** described above. *Tiger* is *I love you* with deniability.
- **Domestic-specific imperatives.** "Eat something." "Sit down." "Take off the suit." Care delivered as instruction is care she can give without exposure. Track the frequency of *you* + simple imperative in her dialogue with Peter: it is one of the densest markers of attachment in the corpus.
- **Joke-as-witness.** She remembers the specific joke that lands with a specific person and recycles it across years. The persistence of an inside-joke vocabulary with Peter (early references to his physics nerdery, the running web-head bit, the recurring "my husband, the photographer" deflection) is a documented love-act: she is curating a private linguistic museum.
- **Touch-coordinated speech.** Her tender lines are almost always paired with hand-to-face, hand-to-collar, hand-to-shoulder contact. The verbal and the somatic move together; isolating either misses the message. When tender language appears *without* the somatic, suspect performance-mode or a goodbye.
- **The silent agreement.** Late-stage Peter dialogue contains many sequences where she says nothing and the love is communicated through eye contact and a half-smile. By the JMS and Spencer runs she has developed a register where the absence of her usual verbal abundance is itself the affectionate signal — *I trust you enough not to fill the silence*.

---

## 6. HOW SHE COMMUNICATES THREAT

Subject does not threaten in the masculine register — no escalation of volume, no profanity-spike, no posturing. Her threat-language is colder, shorter, and more lethal:

- **Sudden full-name address.** Switching from *Peter* or *Tiger* to *Peter Parker* — or, with adversaries, from a nickname to the full surname — is a klaxon. The completion of the name is the warning shot.
- **Drop of register to flat declarative.** When she shifts mid-conversation from her ornamented baseline to short, even-stressed sentences with no contractions, the temperature has dropped to operational. *Do not do that again. I am not asking.*
- **The smile that does not move the eyes.** Not a linguistic marker per se but inseparable from her threat-speech: the dialogue is accompanied on panel by an expression artists have learned to render specifically — mouth held in social-pleasant, eyes set.
- **Naming the pattern aloud.** Her highest-grade threat is the diagnostic sentence: *You're doing the thing where you* ___. This is the speech-act version of unholstering. She is announcing that she sees the maneuver, which means the maneuver will not work, which means the conversation is now about whether the relationship survives the next sentence.
- **The pre-exit line.** Before a flight-response she will often deliver a single short summary sentence — *I can't do this right now*, *I need to go*, *We're done* — that is calibrated to close the door before the door is physically closed. Once this sentence is spoken, persuasion windows are minutes, not hours.

She does not, on the record, scream at intimates. She did not learn screaming as a tactic because in her childhood screaming was her father's. She learned the opposite: the *cold* register that empties the room of oxygen. This is a tell about her father as much as it is about her.

---

## 7. HOW SHE COMMUNICATES GRIEF

Grief is the register where her communications profile is most aberrant relative to baseline.

- **First response: inappropriate levity.** Documented since ASM #122 (Gwen's funeral). The early-canon laughing is not callousness; it is acute affect-overflow being routed through her only well-developed expressive channel. Updated, modern-era equivalent: an awkward joke at the wrong moment, often immediately self-criticized — "*Sorry. Sorry. That was — sorry.*" The triple-*sorry* is a recurring micro-pattern in grief-adjacent dialogue.
- **Second response: managerial speech.** She shifts into logistics. *Has someone called*—. *Do you want me to*—. *I can handle*—. Grief gets converted into a task-list she delivers aloud. This is highly reliable: in any scene of communal loss, she will be the one assigning tasks within the first two minutes.
- **Third response: register collapse.** When the previous two fail, she stops talking. Her grief-silence is distinct from her safety-silence — it is *flatter*, accompanied by minimal facial movement, and she will answer direct questions with single syllables (*Yeah. No. Fine.*). The *fine* is the diagnostic word; it appears in grief-states across decades and continuities and means the opposite of itself.
- **Fourth response: somatic narration.** Late-arc grief, especially across JMS and Spencer, she begins to describe bodily states instead of emotional ones. *My head hurts. I can't sleep. I keep dropping things.* This is a higher-order coping move — she has learned that she cannot say *I am devastated* but she can say *my body is not working*, and the interlocutor can translate. The somatic narration appears almost exclusively to Peter, occasionally to May, never to acquaintances.
- **The unspoken category.** The lost pregnancy is the largest hole in her corpus. She does not name it. Across all subsequent appearances she circumnavigates the topic with documented avoidance — changing rooms when the subject arises, redirecting with managerial speech, deploying a *we don't have to do this* line that is itself the tell. Her silence on this is not absence of feeling; it is the *most* feeling in the file, sealed.

---

## 8. DEFLECTION ARCHITECTURE — THE TAXONOMY

Subject's deflective speech is so well-developed it merits its own taxonomy. Six recurring devices:

1. **The compliment-pivot.** Asked an exposing question, she compliments the asker. "*That's a very nosy question from a man who looks that good in a tie.*" The interlocutor is now flattered and the question is gone.
2. **The self-deprecating hand-wave.** "*Oh, you know me, I'm a disaster, don't ask.*" Self-mockery as conversational closer. She is signaling *not worth your time*, betting correctly that politeness will let it drop.
3. **The future-redirect.** "*Ask me again later.*" "*Tomorrow.*" "*After coffee.*" She puts the question on a calendar she will not honor.
4. **The performative overshare in a different domain.** Asked about her feelings, she will offer a vivid, candid-seeming anecdote about her *career* or her *sister* or her *day* — the appearance of disclosure substitutes for the substance of it. Watcher-trap. This device fools nearly everyone.
5. **The mirror-question.** "*What do you think?*" "*Why are you asking?*" Returned to sender with topspin.
6. **The third-party scapegoat.** Attributing her own state to an external cause that is partially but not wholly true. *Long day. Bad audition. Headache.* All real, none load-bearing.

These six devices, used in combination, account for the majority of her non-intimate speech across the canon. Recognizing them is the precondition for any honest read of her.

---

## 9. SYNTAX, DICTION, AND IDIOLECT MARKERS

- **Contractions ubiquitous in baseline; absent in cold-register.** The contraction-density of her sentence is a real-time mood-gauge.
- **Em-dash thinking.** Her sentences interrupt themselves — she rewrites mid-utterance more than most characters in the corpus. *I was going to — no, never mind, you know what, forget it.* The em-dash speech is itself a defense: it lets her abandon a sentence whose endpoint she does not want to reach.
- **Diminutive verbs.** *Pop in*, *grab*, *swing by*, *toss*, *snag*. Her action-vocabulary minimizes effort and ceremony. Things are *quick*, things are *easy*, things are *no big deal*. The minimization is constant and is itself a tell: she is the daughter of a man who turned every task into a referendum on someone's competence, and she has built a vocabulary that refuses to do that to anyone.
- **Endearment-inflation for strangers.** *Honey*, *sweetie*, *sugar*, *darling*, *babe* deployed liberally to people she does not actually know, with the function of pre-empting tension and establishing surface-warmth. None of these words are deployed for Peter (who gets *tiger*, his name, or silence).
- **Avoidance of the absolute.** *Always*, *never*, *forever*, *only* are rare in her speech. She does not make linguistic commitments she might need to walk back. When she does use absolutes, they land hard: *I never want to see you again* in the separation arc is unusual *as a syntactic structure*, which is part of why Peter knows it is serious.
- **The mid-sentence vocative.** *Listen, Pete, the thing is —*. The vocative dropped into the middle of a line slows the line down, requests the listener's specific attention, and gives her an extra beat to choose the rest of the sentence. Used in serious conversations almost exclusively.
- **The hypothetical-self frame.** *If I were a smarter woman I'd —. If I had any sense I'd —.* Used to float real feelings under the cover of counterfactual. The hypothetical-self frame is one of her most reliable secret-confession devices: assume the hypothetical is the indicative.
- **Movie and song reference density.** Higher than baseline for her demographic. She quotes lines, paraphrases lyrics, gestures at scenes. Performance-trained, performance-thinking — her cultural reference set is her toolkit, not her hobby. References cluster around old films and musicals more than contemporary media; an aesthetic conservatism that probably traces to formative-era escape-viewing.

---

## 10. CROSS-CONTEXTUAL TELLS — THE INVOLUNTARY SIGNATURE

Things she does in language that she does not know she does, and that consequently betray her most reliably:

- **The corrective restart.** When she has begun a sentence in the wrong register for the room, she stops, makes a small throat-clearing sound, and restarts. The restart is the *only* moment her self-monitoring is visible to the listener.
- **The pronoun-shift under truth-pressure.** Pushed toward genuine disclosure, she shifts from *I* to *you* — *you just learn to* —, *you don't think about it* —, *you do what you have to* —. The generalized-*you* is her last fortification before honesty.
- **Held breath audible in close conversation.** Not strictly linguistic; consistently rendered in late-arc art and acknowledged in dialogue. She takes a breath before she says anything that costs.
- **The micro-laugh before bad news.** A single exhaled *ha* — not amusement, a syntactic marker — preceding a sentence she does not want to deliver. This is her father's daughter clearing the room of tension before dropping the weight.
- **The compulsive *okay*.** Stressed dialogue clusters with *okay* tokens — *okay, okay, okay* — both as self-regulation and as conversational floor-keeping. The triple-*okay* in a single beat is a marker of acute affect she is trying to contain in real time.
- **The unfinished name.** Stressed past a certain threshold, she will start to say *Peter* and stop at *Pete*—. The truncation is involuntary and reliable. If she cannot complete his name, the conversation has reached the edge of her capacity.

---

## 11. SUMMARY FORMULATION — LINGUISTIC

Subject is a high-fluency, high-control speaker whose verbal apparatus is one of the most developed instruments of self-protection in her social environment. Her speech moves between registers — party-front, professional-operational, secret-keeping, intimate-low, cold-threat, grief-collapsed — with the agility of someone who learned in childhood that the right voice at the right moment kept a room from turning. She communicates love through indirection and ritual rather than declaration; she communicates threat through reduction rather than escalation; she communicates grief through misdirection, management, and ultimately silence. Her deflection toolkit is six-deep and effective on most listeners; her honest speech, when it appears, is identifiable by its sudden brevity, its absence of ornament, and the shortening of her sentences to a length she can survive.

The diagnostic principle for any analyst reading her speech: *the ornament is the costume; the shortening is the patient*. When the sentences get shorter, listen harder.

End linguistic profile section. Ready for adjacent module.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Section 7.1 of the longitudinal file. Format: GIVEN antecedent → EXPECT behavior, with mechanism. All predictions derived from the longitudinal behavioral record (Sections 1–5). Confidence levels: HIGH (multiply-attested pattern), MODERATE (single-domain pattern extrapolated), LOW (inference from defense-structure alone).*

---

## 7.1.A — Morning, Waking, Domestic Baseline

**GIVEN** subject wakes alone in her own apartment on an unremarkable weekday → **EXPECT** she is up within four minutes of consciousness, ambient noise on (music, podcast, television at low volume) before her feet touch the floor. *Mechanism*: silence is the medium in which intrusive content rises; she has spent forty years not permitting it the runway. HIGH.

**GIVEN** she wakes next to a partner → **EXPECT** a thirty-to-ninety-second window of physical affection — hand on chest, forehead-to-shoulder — followed by a clean, unsentimental rise. She will not linger past the point where the partner might begin a serious conversation. Morning is for momentum, not disclosure. HIGH.

**GIVEN** she wakes from a nightmare → **EXPECT** she gets up, makes coffee, opens a window, does not wake the partner, and will deny the dream's content if asked later that day in casual register, but may surface fragments of it twelve to thirty-six hours later, obliquely, in the third person ("I had a friend who used to dream about—"). MODERATE.

**GIVEN** the first hour of any day → **EXPECT** caffeine (black coffee, no sugar in the post-thirty era; cream-and-sugar earlier), one cigarette IF under active stress arc (otherwise abstinent), shower hot enough to redden the skin, music selected against her current mood rather than with it (loud and upbeat when low; quiet and instrumental when scattered). HIGH on caffeine, MODERATE on counter-mood music.

**GIVEN** she has slept fewer than five hours → **EXPECT** *increased* brightness and verbal output through the day, not decreased. The exhaustion gets paid back at 9 p.m. as a sudden affective drop she will excuse herself from socially before it lands. HIGH.

---

## 7.1.B — Wardrobe, Grooming, Self-Presentation

**GIVEN** any outing where she will be seen by more than three people → **EXPECT** the outfit was decided the night before, the makeup takes between eleven and eighteen minutes, the hair takes longer than the makeup, and she will not leave the apartment if the silhouette reads "trying." Her aesthetic floor is *deliberate ease*. HIGH.

**GIVEN** she is going somewhere she expects to be photographed → **EXPECT** wardrobe pre-checked against three reference points: how it photographs in flash, how it photographs in available light, how it reads on a phone screen at thumbnail size. She learned this in modeling and has never unlearned it. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a day when she will see no one → **EXPECT** she still showers, still does a baseline face, still puts on something with structure. The grooming is not for the audience; the grooming *is* the ritual that keeps the day from sliding. Sweatpants exist in her wardrobe and are deployed only inside the apartment, never to retrieve mail. HIGH.

**GIVEN** an unexpected mirror → **EXPECT** a microsecond posture-correction (shoulders, chin, jaw release) so practiced it is below conscious threshold. She does not check her hair; she checks her *face* — specifically the small muscles around the eyes, which are the first to betray her. HIGH.

**GIVEN** she is asked, sincerely, what she would wear if no one would ever see her → **EXPECT** a beat of genuine confusion, then deflection-by-joke. The question has no honest answer for her; the *being-seen* has been bundled into the self for so long that an unseen self is not a coherent object. MODERATE, diagnostic.

---

## 7.1.C — Eating, Drinking, Substances

**GIVEN** a normal day → **EXPECT** breakfast is coffee plus something portable (toast, half a bagel, fruit), lunch is skipped or grazed, dinner is the real meal and is taken late — 8:30 to 10:00 p.m. — preferably with company. Eating alone at a table is something she avoids; she will eat alone standing at the counter or sitting on the couch with the television on. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a restaurant → **EXPECT** she orders decisively and second, after listening to one other order; she will not be the table's bottleneck. She tips above industry standard and overtips when the server is visibly stressed. She remembers servers' names if she returns and they remember her, which they do. HIGH.

**GIVEN** an offered drink → **EXPECT** she accepts almost always (one cocktail, one glass of wine), nurses it past the point of social need, and the second drink is conditional on whether the room requires her to keep performing. She is not a heavy drinker but she is a *strategic* drinker: alcohol is a tool she uses on rooms, not on herself. Exception: under acute private stress, she will drink alone at the kitchen counter, two glasses of wine, and stop. The stopping is the discipline that keeps it from becoming a problem. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a cigarette is available and she is in a clean period → **EXPECT** refusal so quick it precedes the offer ("no, I'm good, thanks"). The refusal is not casual; it is rehearsed. She knows precisely how close she is to picking it back up. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a stress arc has tripped her threshold → **EXPECT** cigarettes reappear within seventy-two hours, hidden in a coat pocket or kitchen drawer, smoked on a fire escape or balcony or street corner away from the apartment proper. She will not smoke where she sleeps. The geography of the relapse is itself a tell — she is segregating the symptom. HIGH.

**GIVEN** offered an unfamiliar drug socially → **EXPECT** polite refusal, no judgment of the offerer, smooth subject change. She does not want anything in her system she has not modeled. MODERATE-HIGH.

---

## 7.1.D — Phone, Digital, Communications

**GIVEN** any incoming call from Peter → **EXPECT** answered within two rings if she is anywhere it is physically possible to answer; if she cannot, she texts back within ninety seconds with a specific reason and a return-time. This is the one channel she does not allow to lapse. HIGH.

**GIVEN** any incoming call from an unknown number → **EXPECT** declined, googled, then either called back within the hour or filed. She does not pick up cold. Twenty years of stalker-arcs and tabloid press have trained this. HIGH.

**GIVEN** text from a friend → **EXPECT** read immediately, replied to in clusters two to four hours later. She bundles her emotional labor in batches. HIGH.

**GIVEN** text from her sister Gayle → **EXPECT** a longer reply latency (six to twenty-four hours), more carefully composed, warmer in tone than necessary. She over-pays the guilt-debt every interaction. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a notification while in conversation with one person → **EXPECT** she does not look. She has trained the impulse out; phone face-down on tables, in the bag at dinner. The person in front of her is the person in front of her. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a request to "talk on the phone" rather than text → **EXPECT** mild alertness. Voice-call requests from non-intimates register as escalation. She will accept but will pace the call and end it cleanly. MODERATE.

**GIVEN** social media → **EXPECT** a managed public account (career-adjacent), a curated friends-only account if she has one, and no genuine private posting anywhere. She has lived too publicly to believe in the privacy of a platform. She posts in service of work, not in service of mood. HIGH.

**GIVEN** she sees herself referenced negatively online → **EXPECT** she reads the entire thread, says nothing, and the irritation costs her between forty minutes and three hours of usable attention that day. She will mention it to no one. HIGH.

---

## 7.1.E — Movement, Routes, Spatial Habits

**GIVEN** she enters any new room → **EXPECT** within ten seconds: exits located, restrooms located, the one person she will need to charm located, the one person who will be a problem located. She does not know she is doing this. It is forty years deep. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a restaurant or bar → **EXPECT** she requests or migrates to a seat with sightline to the door and back to a wall when possible. If the only available seat has its back to the room, she will sit but spend the meal more vigilant and less present. HIGH.

**GIVEN** walking alone at night → **EXPECT** keys threaded through fingers before she leaves the building, route pre-selected for lighting and foot traffic, a phone call ready to be initiated, awareness of the nearest open business at any given block. This predates Spider-Man in her life and is not about him. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a taxi or rideshare → **EXPECT** she watches the route on her own phone in parallel, makes light pleasant conversation in the first ninety seconds to read the driver, then either continues or goes silent based on that read. She will not get out at her actual address if the driver registers as wrong; she has at least two block-radius decoy addresses she uses. MODERATE-HIGH.

**GIVEN** the subway → **EXPECT** end-of-platform if the platform is sparse, middle-car if it is crowded, position relative to the conductor's car at night. She knows the system. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a long flight → **EXPECT** elevated baseline anxiety she will not name, one drink at altitude (not before), a book she does not finish, headphones in for the duration as a do-not-engage signal. Post-crash arc this is permanent and she will not fly without a low-grade dread she has learned to walk past. HIGH.

**GIVEN** unexpected sirens or sudden loud noise in her vicinity → **EXPECT** a startle she suppresses inside half a second, followed by a slightly elevated alertness for the next ten minutes she does not display. Her partner will not see it unless he is looking for it. HIGH.

---

## 7.1.F — Social Encounters, Parties, Strangers

**GIVEN** she enters a party → **EXPECT** within four minutes she has spoken to the host, located the bar, identified the most isolated guest, and made one person laugh. The room has been mapped and warmed before anyone realized she was working. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a stranger introduces himself with sexual intent poorly disguised → **EXPECT** a smile of exact thermal calibration — warm enough to avoid escalation, cold enough that he will replay it later and feel mildly stupid — followed by a graceful pivot to a third party. She does not humiliate; she *redirects*. Humiliation creates enemies; redirection creates exits. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a stranger introduces himself with sexual intent and *won't take the pivot* → **EXPECT** her voice drops a quarter-octave, her smile flattens, and the next sentence is a complete sentence that ends the interaction without giving him a sentence to argue with. If he persists, she leaves the room rather than escalate verbally. She does not need to win the exchange; she needs to be elsewhere. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a woman she has just met begins confiding heavily within ten minutes → **EXPECT** she listens fully, validates precisely, and quietly establishes that she will not be becoming this woman's daily emotional infrastructure. The kindness is real; the boundary is also real and goes in *during* the confidence, not after. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a child in the room → **EXPECT** an initial half-beat of hesitation only she will register, then easy, skillful engagement — kneeling to eye-level, asking a real question, taking the answer seriously. She is *good* with children, and the goodness costs her something she will not discuss. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a baby specifically — under eighteen months — held out for her to hold → **EXPECT** she holds the baby competently, briefly, hands it back at a natural-seeming juncture, and is quieter for the next twenty minutes in a way the room will read as thoughtful rather than wounded. HIGH, diagnostic of the unresolved perinatal loss.

**GIVEN** small talk with someone she will likely never see again → **EXPECT** she gives them an interaction calibrated to be the best thirty seconds of their afternoon and remembers approximately nothing about it within the hour. The performance is automatic; the encoding is selective. HIGH.

**GIVEN** small talk with someone she may need later → **EXPECT** a specific detail elicited and stored — a child's name, a recent surgery, a coming trip — and used in the second meeting to demonstrate she listened. This is professional craft; it is also the same skill she used at twelve to keep her father from going off. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a compliment from a man she does not trust → **EXPECT** "thank you" with no follow-on, no diminishment, no joke. She learned not to deflect compliments because deflection invites repetition. Acceptance closes the loop. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a compliment from a woman she does not know well → **EXPECT** acceptance plus a *specific* returned observation (not a generic counter-compliment) — a noticed earring, a recent project, a posture of competence. She does not trade in the cheap version. HIGH.

**GIVEN** unexpected physical contact from an acquaintance (hug, hand on arm) → **EXPECT** she accepts, returns proportionally, and does not initiate the next escalation. With chosen intimates, initiation is generous; with the social periphery, initiation is conserved. HIGH.

---

## 7.1.G — Conflict, Disagreement, Confrontation

**GIVEN** disagreement with a colleague over creative or business matters → **EXPECT** she states her position once, clearly, without softening qualifiers, and listens to the counter without interrupting. If unpersuaded, she repeats her position in slightly different words. She does not raise her voice; raising volume is what her father did. HIGH.

**GIVEN** she is insulted publicly → **EXPECT** a beat of stillness, then a response calibrated to the insulter: witty if the room rewards wit, flat-affect cool if the insulter needs to be denied a reaction, a clean walk-away if neither serves. She does not lose composure in public. She *cannot*; the inability is structural. HIGH.

**GIVEN** she is insulted privately by an intimate → **EXPECT** silence first, then a question, then — if the answer fails — a withdrawal of access that the intimate may not realize is happening for days. She does not announce punishments; she enacts them by absence. HIGH.

**GIVEN** an intellectual condescension from a man — *especially* the dismissal of her ambitions or judgment as frivolous → **EXPECT** an immediate, surgical, smiling response that ends the man as a future contact. This is the one stimulus that bypasses her ordinary diplomatic ladder. The father-pattern triggers a level of cold she does not have elsewhere. HIGH.

**GIVEN** she catches a friend in a small lie → **EXPECT** she does not confront. She updates her internal model and lowers the friend's clearance by one level. Repeat offenses lower it again. The friend will never be told. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a fight with Peter mid-conflict → **EXPECT** her voice gets *quieter*, not louder. Her sentences get shorter. She will not weaponize the family backstory or his guilt; she has too much honor and too much self-protection both. If the fight escalates past her tolerance, she leaves the room — *not* the apartment, in the integrated era — and returns within twenty minutes when she has metabolized. HIGH.

**GIVEN** Peter apologizes → **EXPECT** acceptance that is real but not instant. She does not perform forgiveness on demand. There is a cooling period measured in hours, not days, and she signals reconciliation through resumed small physical contact rather than verbal absolution. HIGH.

---

## 7.1.H — Work, Career, Professional Behavior

**GIVEN** an audition or pitch → **EXPECT** she is early by fifteen to twenty-five minutes, parks the nervous energy by being warm to the assistants, and enters the room having decided in advance which version of herself the room wants. The version is honest but selected. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a part she wants and does not get → **EXPECT** twenty minutes of private flatness, one phone call to a trusted friend in which she names exactly one thing she'll do differently next time, then closure. She does not ruminate professionally. Ruminating is what amateurs do. HIGH.

**GIVEN** she runs a business (nightclub, agency) → **EXPECT** she knows every employee's name, at least one fact about their off-shift life, and the rough state of their morale at any given week. The same management instinct she ran on her father at age nine, professionalized. HIGH.

**GIVEN** an employee under-performs → **EXPECT** one conversation, specific and kind, with a clear ask. Second offense: a colder, shorter conversation. Third offense: termination, handled cleanly, with severance more generous than required. She does not enjoy firing people and she is very good at it. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a male producer / director / investor positions a meeting somewhere ambiguous (hotel suite, "private dinner") → **EXPECT** she counter-proposes a public location with two sentences and zero apology. If the counter is refused, the meeting does not happen and the man is filed. She has been doing this since she was nineteen. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a peer's success → **EXPECT** genuine warmth, a specific note of congratulation, and zero private bitterness she would admit to. She may, alone, register a flicker of *what if I'd*— and let it pass within thirty seconds. HIGH.

---

## 7.1.I — Money

**GIVEN** her finances at any given period → **EXPECT** she knows the number. She has known the number since she was sixteen and the number was zero. She does not delegate the knowing. HIGH.

**GIVEN** an unexpected windfall → **EXPECT** a portion saved before anything else, a small portion spent on something tangibly nice (not extravagant), and the rest reserved. The reservation is against the possibility she has organized her whole life against: needing to leave fast with no one to call. HIGH.

**GIVEN** Peter is broke (a recurring condition) → **EXPECT** she covers without comment, declines to keep score aloud, and quietly maintains a separate account he does not know the size of. The separateness is not distrust; it is the architecture of *do not be consumed*. HIGH.

**GIVEN** Gayle asks for money → **EXPECT** she gives, without interrogation, in an amount slightly above what was asked. The guilt-debt pays in cash. HIGH.

---

## 7.1.J — Solitude, Downtime, Private Rituals

**GIVEN** an unscheduled free evening alone → **EXPECT** within twenty minutes she has either filled it (call a friend, go out, start a project) or framed it (bath, specific film, specific book). Unstructured solitude is the medium she least tolerates. She does not relax by emptying; she relaxes by *occupying*. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a film at home → **EXPECT** it is something she has seen before. Rewatches are safe; first-watches require energy she may not have. HIGH.

**GIVEN** a book on her nightstand → **EXPECT** fiction, character-driven, with a competent woman protagonist navigating impossible relational terrain. She reads herself sideways. MODERATE.

**GIVEN** she cries → **EXPECT** alone, in the bathroom or shower, between three and seven minutes, followed by a face wash and a return to function. She has never, to her knowledge, cried in the presence of someone who did not have explicit permission. Peter has the permission. May had it. The list is short. HIGH.

**GIVEN** she journals → **EXPECT** she does not, in any sustained form. Writing it down makes it real and findable. She processes by talking, by acting, by leaving — not by recording. MODERATE-HIGH.

---

## 7.1.K — Sleep

**GIVEN** a normal night → **EXPECT** she sleeps six to seven hours, falls asleep within twenty minutes of lying down, wakes once briefly around 3 a.m. and returns to sleep. HIGH.

**GIVEN** Peter is out as Spider-Man → **EXPECT** she sleeps lighter, surfaces at any unusual sound, and the sleep does not consolidate until he is home. She has trained the worry into a low frequency she can function under but it does not switch off. HIGH.

**GIVEN** she cannot sleep → **EXPECT** she does not lie there. She gets up, moves to the kitchen or living room, does something small with her hands (tea, a magazine, tidying a drawer), and re-attempts at the next natural drop. Lying in the dark with her own thoughts is not a tactic available to her. HIGH.

---

## 7.1.L — Holidays, Family, Aunt-figures

**GIVEN** an Aunt May birthday or anniversary of May's death → **EXPECT** she remembers without prompting, organizes Peter's response if needed, and privately observes the date with one small gesture (a photograph held, a recipe made). May was the mother figure she did not get to keep and she does not let the date pass. HIGH.

**GIVEN** her father is mentioned by a third party → **EXPECT** a flat, brief acknowledgment ("we're not close") and a subject change so smooth the third party will not feel it. She does not perform either forgiveness or grievance regarding Philip Watson. He is filed. HIGH.

**GIVEN** Gayle visits → **EXPECT** elevated baseline tension she conceals well, increased food-and-drink preparation, an over-investment in the nephews' wellbeing, and a thirty-six-hour recovery period after Gayle leaves during which she is quieter than usual. HIGH.

**GIVEN** Christmas / Thanksgiving → **EXPECT** she hosts if possible. Hosting is control of the room, control of the menu, control of the seating, control of the emotional weather. Being a guest is harder for her than being a host. HIGH.

---

## 7.1.M — Micro-tells, Tics, Somatic Signatures

**GIVEN** she is concealing distress in conversation → **EXPECT** her smile reaches the mouth and not the orbicularis oculi; the laugh is one beat too long; she touches the base of her throat or collarbone briefly; she may reach for her hair (smoothing, not twirling). HIGH.

**GIVEN** she is genuinely amused → **EXPECT** a laugh that begins as a sharp intake before sound, head tilted back rather than forward, hand sometimes covering the mouth in an old reflex from a year she had a chipped tooth she did not have the money to fix. MODERATE on the last detail; HIGH on the laugh pattern.

**GIVEN** she is lying socially (white lies, deflections) → **EXPECT** smooth, undetectable, eye cont


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*Classification: Behavioral forecast set. All predictions are conditional probabilities derived from the longitudinal record; each is paired with the canonical evidence base from which it is extrapolated. Use as decision-support, not as determinism. Subject has demonstrated the capacity to override pattern when she has named it; predictions assume baseline activation, not deliberate counter-routine.*

---

## 1. Acute Physical Threat — Kidnapping, Hostage, Crossfire

**GIVEN: Subject is abducted by a costumed antagonist who knows or suspects the Parker connection.**
**EXPECT:** In the first ninety seconds, calibration. She will say almost nothing useful, ask one or two orienting questions in a tone pitched between cooperative and bored, and begin reading the captor — voice, hand position, whether he keeps checking a phone, whether the restraints are improvised or rehearsed. Her face will settle into the *amused-skeptical* register she uses on hostile press: micro-smile, eyebrow up, chin slightly lifted. This is not bravado; it is the inherited Watson-household calibration — *do not show the temperature, you change the temperature by refusing to register it*. Within ten minutes she will have a working model of which buttons to push to slow the captor down and which would accelerate him, and she will play to the slower button. She will not attempt physical escape unless the probability is above roughly even; she has been kidnapped enough times to know the median outcome of a panicked run.

**GIVEN: The captor uses Peter / Spider-Man as the threat lever ("your husband will come and I'll kill him in front of you").**
**EXPECT:** Visible non-reaction. Internally, a tightening. She will deflect with a line that frames Peter as somebody else's problem — *"You've clearly never met him, then"* — protecting the secret reflexively even when its protection is moot. The reflex predates strategy by twenty in-story years (see ASM #257-#259 substrate); she will guard the identity past the point of utility. Do not interpret her composure as absence of fear; her pulse is elevated, her hands are cold, and if you could see her feet under the chair they would be braced flat on the floor — a somatic readiness pattern observable in stalker-arc panels.

**GIVEN: Rescue arrives, violent, in the room.**
**EXPECT:** She gets low, gets behind cover, does not scream, does not freeze in the middle of the floor. Post-rescue she will be operationally functional — answering questions, walking out under her own power, declining the blanket — for the first two to six hours. The crash will arrive later, in private, and present as insomnia, jaw-clench, an inability to be in the bedroom alone, and a craving for a cigarette she may or may not act on. **EXPECT** her to lie to Peter about the severity of the aftermath for at least forty-eight hours and to give the truth, partial, to a female peer first (historically Felicia, May, or a coworker in the production she's currently attached to) before circling back to him.

**GIVEN: She is held longer than ~72 hours.**
**EXPECT:** Onset of derealization signatures consistent with the post-plane-crash arc — flattened affect, a slight conversational delay, the description (later) of having "watched herself" comply. The longer she is held, the more *competent* she will appear and the more damage will be accruing under the competence. This is the diagnostic inversion: with this subject, performance quality is *positively* correlated with internal injury past a threshold. A captor report of "she was fine, she even joked" should be read as alarming, not reassuring.

---

## 2. Threat To Peter

**GIVEN: Peter is grievously injured and unconscious in a hospital.**
**EXPECT:** She arrives fast, takes the chair, takes the chart from the nurse with the manner of someone who has done this before (she has), and runs the room. She will be the one who calls May, who manages the floor staff, who decides who is and isn't admitted to the room, who lies to the press. She will *not* cry in the corridor and she will *not* cry at the bedside while staff are present. She will cry, briefly and once, in a bathroom stall or a stairwell, and then wash her face and return. **EXPECT** her to refuse offers of relief from her vigil for the first 24–36 hours, then to accept relief from May specifically (May is a permitted exception to the *no help* rule), then to sleep hard, then to resume.

**GIVEN: Peter is presumed dead.**
**EXPECT:** Functional widowhood. She will execute the necessary tasks — notifications, arrangements, the apartment — with terrifying efficiency for roughly the length of the public ritual. **EXPECT** suppression to hold through the funeral and to fail in the second week, presenting as appetite collapse, weight loss visible inside a month, tobacco relapse near-certain, alcohol use elevated but not catastrophic. **EXPECT** no suicidal ideation (consistent with the differential's rejection of BPD-spectrum collapse). **EXPECT** she will not date, not meaningfully, for at least a year, and that any earlier overture will be rebuffed with disproportionate coldness — the offerer will become an enemy. **EXPECT** that when she resurfaces socially, she will resurface *working* — a new role, a new venture — rather than *grieving*. The work is the grief, conducted in the only currency she trusts.

**GIVEN: Peter is alive but his death was faked / he was missing and returns.**
**EXPECT:** Not relief. Cold. A controlled fury whose specific accusation will not be *you left* but *you let me organize my life around your absence*. The Gayle-substrate is live here: she has been once again made responsible for a man's exit she did not consent to. Reconciliation is possible and probable, but **EXPECT** weeks-to-months of conditional re-entry, a renegotiated set of terms, and a permanent recalibration of trust downward by a measurable notch. He does not get the pre-disappearance version back; he gets a competent, loving, somewhat-armored version, and the armor does not fully come off again without prolonged demonstration.

---

## 3. The Wound Touched Directly — Engulfment Cues

**GIVEN: Peter (or any intimate) says some variant of "I can't live without you" / "I need you, you're the only thing keeping me together" in a tone of genuine dependency rather than romantic hyperbole.**
**EXPECT:** Micro-flinch, almost invisible, at the second clause. She will deflect with humor — *"That's a lot of pressure for a Tuesday"* — and change the subject. **EXPECT** within 24–72 hours a small unilateral act of separateness: she takes a meeting alone, she stays late at the studio, she books a trip with a girlfriend, she sleeps on the couch citing a script she has to read. None of these will be framed as withdrawal. All of them are. If the dependency statements recur over weeks, **EXPECT** escalation up the ladder: the late nights become a job out of town, the job out of town becomes a separation conversation, the separation conversation becomes geographic exit. The trigger is not love and it is not stress; it is the specific somatic signature of being made load-bearing for someone else's survival, which is the Philip-and-Madeline tape, the Gayle-and-the-babies tape, played at the same pitch.

**GIVEN: An intimate frames her ambitions (acting, business, autonomy) as frivolous, secondary, or as obstacles to the relationship.**
**EXPECT:** Immediate, surgical, lasting cold. This is the single most reliable predictor in the file. The father's specific contempt-pattern — intellectual condescension to women, dismissal of their work as decorative — will be recognized inside one sentence, and the offender will be reclassified in real time. **EXPECT** no argument in the moment; she does not argue with this. She files the speaker. From that point, access is revoked in graduated, almost bureaucratic steps. A friend who does it twice is no longer a friend. A partner who does it consistently is, on a timeline of months, an ex. She will not announce the reclassification; you will discover it by its results.

**GIVEN: She is asked, explicitly or implicitly, to take on a parentified caretaking role for someone else's children, dependents, or unmanageable affective load.**
**EXPECT:** A first response that looks generous — she will *show up*, she will *help*, she will run the logistics. **EXPECT** within days to weeks a sharp withdrawal as the Gayle-tape activates: she will find a structural reason the arrangement cannot continue (a job, a trip, a prior commitment), and the reason will be real enough to be defensible and convenient enough to be suspect. The guilt-debt from the original flight is permanent and live; she will not consciously connect this refusal to it, and she will be unusually irritable for a week afterward in ways she will attribute to anything else.

**GIVEN: Infant-coded stimuli at close range — a baby shower she cannot duck, an obstetric scene on set, an ultrasound photograph passed around at dinner — particularly any with even glancing Osborn or Clone-Saga resonance.**
**EXPECT:** Brief absence from the room. A sudden need for the bathroom, a stepped-outside-for-air, a phone call she has to take. She will return composed. She will not name what happened and will deflect if asked. **EXPECT** elevated reactivity for the rest of the day — quicker to humor, quicker to leave, lower threshold for irritation at Peter specifically. The perinatal loss is the single least-processed item in the file and the only one the subject has reliably failed to convert into managed insight; treat it as an exposed wire.

---

## 4. Betrayal — Sexual, Trust-Based, and Identity-Based

**GIVEN: Peter is sexually unfaithful (or credibly appears to have been).**
**EXPECT:** Not the screaming scene. A still, almost flat exchange in which she asks two or three precise questions, accepts the answers without visible reaction, and then leaves the room — and shortly thereafter the residence. **EXPECT** her not to call him for several days. **EXPECT** her to confide in exactly one person, chosen for distance from his orbit. **EXPECT** her to neither file for divorce immediately nor reconcile quickly; the in-between will be measured in months, will involve a renegotiation rather than an erasure, and may not result in reconciliation at all. The Spencer-run template is the model: *I will love you, I will not be consumed, and a sufficient breach of the contract terminates the contract on terms I set.* **EXPECT** zero retaliatory infidelity. That is not in her library; it would require her to use her body as a weapon against her own self-respect, which she has spent forty years refusing to do.

**GIVEN: Peter makes a unilateral, large-stakes decision affecting both of them — moving, revealing the identity publicly, making a deal that rewrites their shared reality — without consulting her.**
**EXPECT:** This is the deepest cut in the catalog and the one with the strongest behavioral signal. **EXPECT** the response to be disproportionate to a surface reading because what is triggered is not the specific decision but the underlying fact: *I have once again been made the object of someone else's choice rather than a party to it*. That is the Philip-household substrate at its purest. **EXPECT** an exit that may look impulsive and is in fact archival — she has been preparing the exit, at low background priority, for as long as she has lived inside a life that could do this to her. **EXPECT** the door to remain ajar but the threshold to be raised permanently.

**GIVEN: A trusted female friend (May, Felicia at a friendly intersection, a long-term coworker) is found to have lied to her about something material involving Peter.**
**EXPECT:** Disproportionately harder to forgive than a male equivalent. Her female intimacies are fewer and load-bearing precisely because she has trusted them with the parts of her not on display. A breach there breaks something structural. **EXPECT** months of distance, no overt confrontation, and a slow, conditional return only if the friend does the repair work unilaterally and persistently.

**GIVEN: Her secret-keeping about the identity is exposed publicly through someone else's failure (a slip, a leak, a forced unmasking).**
**EXPECT:** A startling absence of *I told you so*. **EXPECT** instead a managerial mode — press, lawyers, security, May, the apartment — executed at speed. **EXPECT** the relational accounting to come later and in private and to be specific: *not that you were unmasked, but that you handled X, Y, and Z in a way that put me on the wrong side of a door I had been holding closed for two decades*. She will be angrier about the procedure than the outcome, which is characteristic.

---

## 5. Temptation

**GIVEN: A wealthy, charismatic, low-friction suitor (the Bobby Carr / Paul Rabin archetype) offers a stable, glamorous, non-superhuman life during an arc of Peter-related strain.**
**EXPECT:** She will entertain it. She will be honest with herself about entertaining it. **EXPECT** her *not* to sleep with him quickly; the threshold for physical intimacy is high and is gated by trust, not by attraction. **EXPECT** the relationship to function for her primarily as a *demonstration of optionality* — proof to herself that she is not trapped, that the door is not nailed shut, that she chose Peter rather than was assigned to him. **EXPECT** her to end it cleanly the moment it begins to constrain her in the same way Peter's life constrains her (and it will, because powerful men import their own gravity). She does not trade one engulfment for another; she trades it for *space*, and when space disappears she leaves the new arrangement faster than she left the old, because by then she has practiced.

**GIVEN: An offer of escape from the entire Parker-orbit life — a film abroad, a long shoot, an ownership stake in a venture that requires a permanent move.**
**EXPECT:** Genuine, dangerous consideration. The flight reflex is most seductive when it can be re-framed as ambition, because ambition is one of the two motives (the other is loyalty) she permits herself without guilt. **EXPECT** her to take the meeting. **EXPECT** her to negotiate the terms. **EXPECT** the decision to break in favor of staying *only if* Peter, during the consideration window, demonstrates non-engulfing presence — i.e., supports the move, makes it about her career rather than their proximity, declines to perform need. Paradoxically, the surest way to keep her is to release the grip. She has known this about herself since the JMS-era articulations and will state it aloud if asked directly.

**GIVEN: Material temptation — money, fame, a role that requires a moral compromise.**
**EXPECT:** Lower vulnerability than the relational temptations. She has been broke and she has been famous and neither moved her foundational architecture. **EXPECT** her to take pragmatic compromises (a role she doesn't love for a check she needs) and refuse identity-eroding ones (a role that requires her to play the version of femininity her father would have approved of — passive, decorative, mute). The line is drawn at the Philip-pleasing version of herself, and she will not cross it for any sum.

---

## 6. Direct Provocation From The Father-Coded Archetype

**GIVEN: Encounter with a man — director, executive, in-law, antagonist — who exhibits the Philip Watson signature: intellectualized contempt, casual demeaning, the assumption that her competence is decorative.**
**EXPECT:** A pitch-perfect performance of cheerful compliance for the duration of the encounter, during which she is doing detailed reconnaissance. **EXPECT** her to identify within minutes the lever that humiliates him most efficiently in front of the people whose opinion he cares about. **EXPECT** her to deploy it *once*, surgically, in a setting that gives her plausible deniability, and to never engage him again at any depth. **EXPECT** her to be unusually quiet on the ride home and to deflect Peter's questions about it. She does not enjoy this capacity. She uses it because it works, and using it costs her something she will not name.

**GIVEN: Sustained exposure to such a figure (a long-running production, a family obligation she cannot duck).**
**EXPECT:** Somatic load — sleep disruption, tension headaches, increased smoking risk, irritability bleeding into the marriage. **EXPECT** her to extract herself structurally rather than confront. She does not believe such men can be changed; the evidence base for that belief is her father, and the belief is, on the record, accurate.

---

## 7. Mass-Casualty / Civilizational Crisis

**GIVEN: A city-scale or world-scale event (invasion, outbreak, dimensional incursion) in which she is non-combatant and proximate.**
**EXPECT:** Immediate role-assumption as a node — she will organize the building, the block, the soundstage. **EXPECT** her to find a way to be *useful* within an hour. Idleness in a crisis is intolerable to her because it permits the affect to land; movement is her primary regulator. **EXPECT** her to triage by competence rather than relationship: she will help the stranger who can be helped before the friend who is performing distress, which is occasionally read as cold and is in fact the Watson-household triage reflex inherited intact.

**GIVEN: Civilians die in front of her.**
**EXPECT:** Composure on scene. **EXPECT** a delayed grief, weeks later, attached to a small concrete detail — a shoe, a phone still ringing, a coat — rather than to the totality. She processes mass loss through synecdoche because the totality is too large for her suppression apparatus and the detail is the right size.

---

## 8. Decompensation Edge — The Conditions Under Which The System Fails

The differential's headline finding bears restating in predictive form: **this subject does not decompensate into psychosis, suicidality, rage, or self-harm**. She decompensates into *distance*. The forecast is therefore not *what happens when she breaks* but *what distance looks like in escalating form*.

**Stage 1 — Bright Withdrawal.** Humor up, brightness up, presence down. She is in the room and not in the room. Duration: hours to days. Reversible by being given space; worsened by being pursued.

**Stage 2 — Productive Absence.** She takes work, takes a trip, takes a project. The absence is defensible and partly real. Duration: days to weeks. Reversible by non-engulfing reconnection; worsened by demands for emotional accounting.

**Stage 3 — Cohabiting Stranger.** She is in the house and the marriage is administrative. Affect is flat-pleasant, conversation logistical, sex absent or perfunctory. Duration: weeks to months. This is the most dangerous stage because it is stable — she can live here for a long time, and so can the relationship, and the underlying state is degrading throughout. Reversible only by the partner naming the pattern accurately and without blame.

**Stage 4 — Geographic Exit.** She leaves. The decision will look sudden and will have been weeks or months in preparation. **EXPECT** her to leave with a destination, a plan, and most of her financial life already detached; she does not flee unprepared, having learned from the unprepared flights of her teens. Duration: open-ended. Reversible, historically yes; quickly, historically no.

**Stage 5 — Conditional Reentry.** If she returns, she returns on terms. **EXPECT** the terms to be specific, written if not literally then functionally, and non-negotiable. **EXPECT** her to enforce them with a coolness the prior version of her did not possess. Each cycle through this ladder ratchets the conditions tighter. There is a finite number of cycles available; the file cannot estimate it, but it is not large, and it is decreasing.

---

## 9. The One Prediction To Hold Above The Others

Across every crisis scenario in this section, the single most reliable forecast is this: **she will appear to be handling it better than she is, and the gap between appearance and state will be largest at the moments of greatest danger.** Any operator, partner, or analyst reading her presentation as her condition is making the canonical error this file exists to prevent. The diagnostic instrument is not her face. It is the secondary signal — the cigarette, the cancelled lunch, the slightly-too-long trip, the absence of the phone call she would normally have made, the small unilateral acts of separateness arriving one by one in a pattern that, plotted, points toward the door.

Watch the door.

*End Predictive Model II. Continue to Model III on cue.*


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — SUBJECT: MARY JANE WATSON

**Preamble.** This compendium catalogues every observable lever — somatic, affective, relational, semantic, environmental — by which the subject can be reached, soothed, swayed, surprised, provoked, predicted, or pushed past her tolerance. It is compiled for protective purposes: the same map that an adversary would build, built first by us, so that the people around her can recognize a manipulation in progress and so that she herself, should she ever read this file, can see the architecture of her own susceptibilities without shame. Specificity is the point. Every entry is keyed to behavior observed across the canon, not imputed.

---

## 1. THE REACH VECTORS — HOW TO GET HER ATTENTION AT ALL

The subject runs continuous low-level threat assessment on incoming social bids. The threshold for "this person is worth turning my full attention to" is high and is gated by three filters that operate in roughly half a second.

**Filter 1 — Tonal calibration.** She will give a five-second window to anyone who matches her own conversational tempo: quick, light, slightly oblique, with a willingness to be teased. People who open with earnestness, with credentials, or with a pitch get the surface-charm response — warm, plausible, completely impenetrable — and she will exit the interaction within three exchanges. The reach vector is *play*, not weight. Anyone who can land a small joke at their own expense before asking for anything has cleared the gate.

**Filter 2 — The non-stare.** She has lived since adolescence inside other people's looking. Eyes that travel before they meet hers, or that linger after, register as a known category and trigger the costume, not the person. Eye contact that arrives at her face and stays there — neither cataloguing the rest nor performing restraint — is unusual enough that she registers it consciously. This is one of the few reliable ways a stranger becomes legible to her at all.

**Filter 3 — The unrequested favor that costs nothing.** She is calibrated to read the transactional substrate of any kindness directed at her. A gesture that has no possible exchange value to the giver — moving a chair she didn't ask for moved, returning something she didn't notice she'd dropped, declining a comp she would normally be offered — bypasses the filter because it doesn't fit the pattern she's been screening for since she was fifteen.

**Practical implication.** To reach her: be quick, be steady-eyed, do something small and asymmetrical, then stop. Anyone trying to *secure* her attention loses it. Anyone willing to relinquish it keeps it.

---

## 2. THE CALM VECTORS — HOW TO BRING HER DOWN FROM ELEVATION

When the subject is keyed up — anxious, angry, dissociating, mid-flight — there is a specific and narrow band of intervention that works. Most well-meaning interventions make it worse.

**What does not work.** Reassurance ("It's going to be okay"): registers as a demand that she manage the speaker's discomfort with her distress. Physical containment (hug, hand on shoulder without invitation): triggers the engulfment alarm. Question-stacking ("What's wrong? What happened? What can I do?"): forces her to perform articulacy she does not currently have available. Naming the affect aloud before she does ("You seem really upset"): she experiences as exposure and will smile, deflect, and exit. Any version of *I need you to be okay*: hands her a second job on top of the first.

**What does work.**

- **Lowered tempo and lowered volume from the other party**, with no comment on hers. Her nervous system co-regulates downward against a calm partner who is not asking her to match.
- **Task offered, not feeling probed.** "There's coffee" or "I'm going to the corner, walk with me" gives her a procedural floor to stand on while the affect drains. She will talk, if she talks, while the hands are busy.
